<b>Footnotes&#160;/&#32;references</b><br /><sup id="cite_ref-AR17-glance_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-glance-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20F2017_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20F2017-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>BP plc</b> (formerly <b>The British Petroleum Company plc</b> and <b>BP Amoco plc</b>) is a British <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a> company headquartered in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. It is one of the world's seven oil and gas "<a href="/wiki/Big_Oil" title="Big Oil">supermajors</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-reut1808_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reut1808-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> whose performance in 2012 made it the world's sixth-largest oil and gas company, the sixth-largest energy company by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a><sup id="cite_ref-PFCEnergy_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFCEnergy-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_by_revenue" class="mw-redirect" title="List of companies by revenue">company with the world's 12th-largest revenue (turnover)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OilGasiQ2013_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OilGasiQ2013-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes2012_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2012-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>  It is a <a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertically integrated</a> company operating in all areas of the oil and gas industry, including <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">production</a>, <a href="/wiki/Refining" title="Refining">refining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midstream" title="Midstream">distribution and marketing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Power_generation" class="mw-redirect" title="Power generation">power generation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trader_(finance)" title="Trader (finance)">trading</a>. It also has <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> interests in <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>.
</p><p>As of  31&#160;December&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, BP had operations in 70&#160;countries worldwide, produced around 3.6&#160;million barrels per day (570,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of <a href="/wiki/Barrel_of_oil_equivalent" title="Barrel of oil equivalent">oil equivalent</a>, and had total proved reserves of 18.441&#160;billion barrels (2.9319<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil equivalent.<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-glance_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-glance-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The company has around 18,300&#160;service stations worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-glance_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-glance-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Its largest division is BP America in the United States. In Russia, BP owns a 19.75% stake in <a href="/wiki/Rosneft" title="Rosneft">Rosneft</a>, the world's largest publicly traded oil and gas company by hydrocarbon reserves and production.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> BP has a primary listing on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100_Index" title="FTSE 100 Index">FTSE 100 Index</a>. It has secondary listings on the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>.
</p><p>BP's origins date back to the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Persian_Oil_Company" title="Anglo-Persian Oil Company">Anglo-Persian Oil Company</a> in 1908, established as a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Burmah_Oil" title="Burmah Oil">Burmah Oil Company</a> to exploit oil discoveries in Iran. In 1935, it became the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Iranian_Oil_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Iranian Oil Company">Anglo-Iranian Oil Company</a> and in 1954 <b>British Petroleum</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-BPhistory-postwar_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPhistory-postwar-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-time020610_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time020610-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 1959, the company expanded beyond the Middle East to Alaska and it was one of the first companies to strike oil in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>. British Petroleum acquired majority control of <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_Ohio" title="Standard Oil of Ohio">Standard Oil of Ohio</a> in 1978. Formerly majority state-owned, the British government privatised the company in stages between 1979 and 1987. British Petroleum merged with <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a> in 1998, becoming <b>BP Amoco plc</b>, and acquired <a href="/wiki/ARCO" title="ARCO">ARCO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burmah_Oil" title="Burmah Oil">Burmah Castrol</a> in 2000, becoming <b>BP plc</b> in 2001. From 2003 to 2013, BP was a partner in the <a href="/wiki/TNK-BP" title="TNK-BP">TNK-BP</a> joint venture in Russia.
</p><p>BP has been directly involved in several major environmental and safety incidents. Among them were the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Texas_City_Refinery_explosion" title="Texas City Refinery explosion">Texas City Refinery explosion</a>, which caused the death of 15&#160;workers and resulted in a record-setting <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">OSHA</a> fine; Britain's largest oil spill, the wreck of <a href="/wiki/SS_Torrey_Canyon" title="SS Torrey Canyon"><i>Torrey Canyon</i></a> in 1967; and the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay_oil_spill" title="Prudhoe Bay oil spill">Prudhoe Bay oil spill</a>, the largest oil spill on <a href="/wiki/Alaska_North_Slope" title="Alaska North Slope">Alaska's North Slope</a>, which resulted in a US$25&#160;million civil penalty, the largest per-barrel penalty at that time for an oil spill.<sup id="cite_ref-Roach2006_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roach2006-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill"><i>Deepwater Horizon</i> oil spill</a>, the largest accidental release of oil into marine waters in history, resulted in severe environmental, health and economic consequences,<sup id="cite_ref-AccidentalRelease_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccidentalRelease-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and serious legal and public relations repercussions for BP. 1.8 million US gallons (43,000&#160;bbl; 6,800&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of <a href="/wiki/Corexit" title="Corexit">Corexit</a> <a href="/wiki/Oil_dispersant" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil dispersant">oil dispersant</a> were used in the cleanup response, becoming the largest application of such chemicals in US history.<sup id="cite_ref-SciAmCorexit_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SciAmCorexit-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>  The company pleaded guilty to 11 counts of felony manslaughter, two misdemeanors, one felony count of lying to Congress, and agreed to pay more than $4.5&#160;billion in fines and penalties, the largest criminal resolution in US history.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian151112_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian151112-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes2012-11_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes2012-11-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BP_fined,_profit_over_prudence_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP_fined,_profit_over_prudence-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On 2 July 2015, BP and five states announced an $18.5 billion settlement to be used for Clean Water Act penalties and various claims.<sup id="cite_ref-abc020715_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc020715-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1909_to_1954">1909 to 1954</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1909 to 1954">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Iranian_Oil_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Iranian Oil Company">Anglo-Iranian Oil Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Petroleum_Company" title="Iraq Petroleum Company">Iraq Petroleum Company</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:213px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Knox_D%27Arcy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/53/William_Knox_D%27Arcy.jpg" width="211" height="267" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="211" data-file-height="267" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Knox_D%27Arcy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Knox_D%27Arcy" title="William Knox D&#39;Arcy">William Knox D'Arcy</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_Motor_Spirit,_1922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/BP_Motor_Spirit%2C_1922.jpg/220px-BP_Motor_Spirit%2C_1922.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/BP_Motor_Spirit%2C_1922.jpg/330px-BP_Motor_Spirit%2C_1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/BP_Motor_Spirit%2C_1922.jpg/440px-BP_Motor_Spirit%2C_1922.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="733" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_Motor_Spirit,_1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A BP Motor Spirit advertisement from 1922</div></div></div>
<p>In May 1908 a group of British geologists discovered a large amount of oil at <a href="/wiki/Masjed_Soleyman_County" title="Masjed Soleyman County">Masjid-i-Suleiman</a> in Mohammerah, today the Iranian province of <a href="/wiki/Khuzestan_Province" title="Khuzestan Province">Khuzestan</a>. It was the first commercially significant find of oil in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>. <a href="/wiki/William_Knox_D%27Arcy" title="William Knox D&#39;Arcy">William Knox D'Arcy</a>, by contract with the Emir of Mohammerah, <a href="/wiki/Khaz%27al_Khan_al-Kaabi" title="Khaz&#39;al Khan al-Kaabi">Sheikh Khaz'al Khan al-Kaabi</a>, obtained permission to explore for oil for the first time in the Middle East,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> an event which changed the history of the entire region. The oil discovery led to petrochemical industry development and also the establishment of industries that strongly depended on oil. On 14 April 1909, the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Persian_Oil_Company" title="Anglo-Persian Oil Company">Anglo-Persian Oil Company</a> (APOC) was incorporated as a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Burmah_Oil" title="Burmah Oil">Burmah Oil Company</a>. Some of the shares were sold to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-Gasson_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gasson-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  The first chairman and minority shareholder of the company became <a href="/wiki/Donald_Smith,_1st_Baron_Strathcona_and_Mount_Royal" title="Donald Smith, 1st Baron Strathcona and Mount Royal">Lord Strathcona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-masjid_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-masjid-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Immediately after establishing the company, the British government asked <a href="/wiki/Percy_Cox" title="Percy Cox">Percy Cox</a>, British resident to <a href="/wiki/Bushehr_Province" title="Bushehr Province">Bushehr</a>, to negotiate an agreement with Khaz'al for APOC to obtain a site on <a href="/wiki/Abadan,_Iran" title="Abadan, Iran">Abadan</a> Island for a refinery, depot, storage tanks, and other operations. The refinery was built and began operating in 1912.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1913, the British government acquired a controlling interest (50.0025%) in the company and at the suggestion of <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, the British navy switched from coal to oil.<sup id="cite_ref-masjid_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-masjid-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc110898_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc110898-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-beale_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beale-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  In 1914, APOC signed a 30-year contract with the <a href="/wiki/British_Admiralty" class="mw-redirect" title="British Admiralty">British Admiralty</a> for supplying oil for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> at the fixed price.<sup id="cite_ref-Atabaki_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atabaki-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  In 1915, APOC established its shipping subsidiary the <a href="/wiki/British_Tanker_Company" title="British Tanker Company">British Tanker Company</a> and in 1916 it acquired the British Petroleum Company which was a marketing arm of the German <i>Europäische Petroleum Union</i> in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-masjid_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-masjid-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  In 1919, the company became a <a href="/wiki/Shale_oil" title="Shale oil">shale-oil</a> producer by establishing a subsidiary named Scottish Oils which merged remaining Scottish <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale_industry" title="Oil shale industry">oil-shale industries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ferrier-shale_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferrier-shale-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marwick_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marwick-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uphall_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uphall-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-museum_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museum-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, APOC started marketing its products in Continental Europe and acquired stakes in the local marketing companies in several European countries. Refineries were built in <a href="/wiki/Llandarcy" title="Llandarcy">Llandarcy</a> in Wales (the first refinery in the United Kingdom) and <a href="/wiki/Grangemouth_Refinery" title="Grangemouth Refinery">Grangemouth</a> in Scotland.  It also acquired the controlling stake in the <a href="/wiki/Courchelettes" title="Courchelettes">Courchelettes</a> refinery in France and formed with the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Australia" title="Government of Australia">Government of Australia</a> a partnership named <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Oil_Refineries" title="Commonwealth Oil Refineries">Commonwealth Oil Refineries</a>, which built the Australian's first refinery in <a href="/wiki/Laverton,_Victoria" title="Laverton, Victoria">Laverton, Victoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-masjid_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-masjid-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  In 1923, Burmah employed <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> as a paid consultant to lobby the British government to allow APOC have exclusive rights to <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Persian</a> oil resources, which were subsequently granted by the Iranian monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-independent030909_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent030909-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>APOC and the Armenian businessman <a href="/wiki/Calouste_Gulbenkian" title="Calouste Gulbenkian">Calouste Gulbenkian</a> were the driving forces behind the creation of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Petroleum_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Petroleum Company">Turkish Petroleum Company</a> (TPC) in 1912 to explore oil in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (now Iraq); and by 1914, APOC held 50% of TPC shares.<sup id="cite_ref-MetzTPC_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetzTPC-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In 1925, TPC received concession in the <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Iraq" title="Oil reserves in Iraq">Mesopotamian oil resources</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq_(Mandate_administration)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Iraq (Mandate administration)">Iraqi government</a> under British mandate. TPC finally struck oil in Iraq on 14 October 1927. By 1928, the APOC's shareholding in TPC, which by now was named <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Petroleum_Company" title="Iraq Petroleum Company">Iraq Petroleum Company</a> (IPC), was reduced to 23.75%; as the result of the changing geopolitics post <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman empire">Ottoman empire</a> break-up, and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_Agreement" title="Red Line Agreement">Red Line Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-1920-78_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-1920-78-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Relations were generally cordial between the pro-west <a href="/wiki/Hashemite_Kingdom_of_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Hashemite Kingdom of Iraq">Hashemite Monarchy (1932–58)</a> in Iraq and IPC, in spite of disputes centered on Iraq's wish for greater involvement and more royalties. During the 1928–68 time period, IPC monopolised oil exploration inside the <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_Agreement" title="Red Line Agreement">Red Line</a>; excluding Saudi Arabia and Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-SH_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SH-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yergin_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yergin-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1927, Burmah Oil and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> formed the joint marketing company <a href="/wiki/Burmah-Shell" class="mw-redirect" title="Burmah-Shell">Burmah-Shell</a>. In 1928, APOC and Shell formed the Consolidated Petroleum Company for sale and marketing in Cyprus, South Africa and Ceylon, which in 1932 followed by a joint marketing company <a href="/wiki/Shell-Mex_and_BP" title="Shell-Mex and BP">Shell-Mex and BP</a> in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrier1982a_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrier1982a-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-beale_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beale-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 1937, AIOC and Shell formed the Shell/D'Arcy Exploration Partners partnership to explore for oil in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. The partnership was equally owned but operated by Shell. It was later replaced by Shell-D'Arcy Petroleum Development Company and Shell-BP Petroleum Development Company (now <a href="/wiki/Shell_Petroleum_Development_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Shell Petroleum Development Company">Shell Petroleum Development Company</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-James2000_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James2000-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1934, APOC and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Oil" title="Gulf Oil">Gulf Oil</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Oil_Company" title="Kuwait Oil Company">Kuwait Oil Company</a> as an equally owned partnership. The oil concession rights were awarded to the company on 23 December 1934 and the company started drilling operations in 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-brune_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brune-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alsharhan_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alsharhan-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  In 1935, <a href="/wiki/Rez%C4%81_Sh%C4%81h" class="mw-redirect" title="Rezā Shāh">Rezā Shāh</a> requested the international community to refer to Persia as '<a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>', which was reflected in the name change of APOC to the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Iranian_Oil_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Iranian Oil Company">Anglo-Iranian Oil Company</a> (AIOC).<sup id="cite_ref-bio_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1947, British Petroleum Chemicals was incorporated as a joint venture of AIOC and <a href="/wiki/The_Distillers_Company" title="The Distillers Company">The Distillers Company</a>.  In 1956, the company was renamed British Hydrocarbon Chemicals.<sup id="cite_ref-James2000c_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James2000c-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following World War II, nationalistic sentiments were on the rise in the Middle East; most notable being <a href="/wiki/Iranian_nationalism" title="Iranian nationalism">Iranian nationalism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arab_Nationalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab Nationalism">Arab Nationalism</a>. In Iran, the AIOC and the pro-western Iranian government led by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ali_Razmara" class="mw-redirect" title="Ali Razmara">Ali Razmara</a> resisted nationalist calls to revise AIOC's concession terms in Iran's favour. In March 1951, Razmara was assassinated and <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Mossadeq" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed Mossadeq">Mohammed Mossadeq</a>, a nationalist, was elected as the new prime minister by the <a href="/wiki/Majlis_of_Iran" class="mw-redirect" title="Majlis of Iran">Majlis of Iran</a> (parliament).<sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-William1991_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-William1991-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In April 1951, the Iranian government <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalised</a> the Iranian oil industry by unanimous vote, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Iranian_Oil_Company" title="National Iranian Oil Company">National Iranian Oil Company</a> (NIOC) was formed, displacing the AIOC.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTRoots_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTRoots-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPHistory_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPHistory-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The AIOC withdrew its management from Iran, and Britain organized an effective worldwide embargo of Iranian oil. The British government, which owned the AIOC, contested the nationalisation at the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, but its complaint was dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-Sztucki_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sztucki-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Prime Minister Churchill asked President Eisenhower for help in overthrowing Mossadeq. The anti-Mossadeq plan was orchestrated under the code-name '<a href="/wiki/Operation_Ajax" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Ajax">Operation Ajax</a>' by CIA, and 'Operation Boot' by <a href="/wiki/Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Secret Intelligence Service">SIS</a> (MI6). The CIA and the British helped stage a coup in August 1953, the <a href="/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1953 Iranian coup d&#39;état">1953 Iranian coup d'état</a>, which established pro-Western general <a href="/wiki/Fazlollah_Zahedi" title="Fazlollah Zahedi">Fazlollah Zahedi</a> as the new PM, and greatly strengthened the political power of Shah <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">Mohammad Reza Pahlavi</a>. The AIOC was able to return to Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1954_to_1979">1954 to 1979</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1954 to 1979">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg/200px-HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg" width="200" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg/300px-HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg/400px-HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2493" data-file-height="2019" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HY_jaune_et_vert2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A BP truck from 1967</div></div></div>
<p>In 1954, the AIOC became the British Petroleum Company. After the <a href="/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1953 Iranian coup d&#39;état">1953 Iranian coup d'état</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Oil_Participants_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian Oil Participants Ltd">Iranian Oil Participants Ltd</a> (IOP), a <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a>, was founded in October 1954 in London to bring Iranian oil back to the international market.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-Vassiliou2009_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-Vassiliou2009-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-Lauterpacht1973_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-Lauterpacht1973-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>  British Petroleum was a founding member of this company with 40% stake.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-William1991_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-William1991-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-Vassiliou2009_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-Vassiliou2009-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>  IOP operated and managed oil facilities in Iran on behalf of NIOC.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-Vassiliou2009_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-Vassiliou2009-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-Lauterpacht1973_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-Lauterpacht1973-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Similar to the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Aramco#History" title="Saudi Aramco">Saudi-Aramco "50/50" agreement of 1950</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ref-B-Christine2008_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-B-Christine2008-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> the consortium agreed to share profits on a 50–50 basis with Iran, "but not to open its books to Iranian auditors or to allow Iranians onto its board of directors."<sup id="cite_ref-Stephen2003_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stephen2003-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1953, British Petroleum entered the Canadian market through the purchase of a minority stake in Calgary-based Triad Oil Company, and expanded further to Alaska in 1959, resulting discovery of oil at <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay_Oil_Field" title="Prudhoe Bay Oil Field">Prudhoe Bay</a> in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-beale_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beale-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-investfairbanks_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investfairbanks-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>  In 1956, its subsidiary D'Arcy Exploration Co. (Africa) Ltd. has been granted four oil concessions in <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj230256_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj230256-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>  In 1962, Scottish Oils ceased <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil-shale</a> operations.<sup id="cite_ref-museum_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museum-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>  In 1965, it was the first company to strike oil in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gulliver_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gulliver-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>  In 1969, BP entered the United States by acquiring the East Coast refining and marketing assets of <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Oil_Corporation" title="Sinclair Oil Corporation">Sinclair Oil Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-James2000b_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James2000b-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The Canadian holding company of British Petroleum was renamed <a href="/wiki/BP_Canada" title="BP Canada">BP Canada</a> in 1969; and in 1971, it acquired 97.8% stake of <a href="/wiki/Supertest_Petroleum" title="Supertest Petroleum">Supertest Petroleum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the 1960s, British Petroleum had developed a reputation for taking on the riskiest ventures. It earned the company massive profits; it also earned them the worst safety record in the industry. In 1967, the giant oil tanker <i><a href="/wiki/Torrey_Canyon" class="mw-redirect" title="Torrey Canyon">Torrey Canyon</a></i> foundered off the English coast. Over 32 million US gallons (760,000&#160;bbl; 120,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of crude oil was spilled into the Atlantic and onto the beaches of Cornwall and Brittany, causing <a href="/wiki/Torrey_Canyon_oil_spill" title="Torrey Canyon oil spill">Britain's worst-ever oil spill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Legacy_of_the_Torrey_Canyon_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Legacy_of_the_Torrey_Canyon-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>  The ship was owned by the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>-based Barracuda Tanker Corporation and was flying the flag of <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, a well-known <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_convenience" title="Flag of convenience">flag of convenience</a>, but was being chartered by British Petroleum.<sup id="cite_ref-Legacy_of_the_Torrey_Canyon_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Legacy_of_the_Torrey_Canyon-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The ship was bombed by <a href="/wiki/RAF" class="mw-redirect" title="RAF">RAF</a> <a href="/wiki/Jet_bomber" class="mw-redirect" title="Jet bomber">jet bombers</a> in an effort to break up the ship and burn off the leaking oil, but this failed to destroy the oil slick.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc290367_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc290367-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1967, BP acquired chemical and plastics assets of The Distillers Company which were merged with British Hydrocarbon Chemicals to form BP Chemicals.<sup id="cite_ref-James2000d_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James2000d-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company's oil assets were nationalised in Libya in 1971, in Kuwait in 1975, and in Nigeria in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-alsharhan_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alsharhan-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPHistory_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPHistory-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-21C-O-01_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-21C-O-01-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In Iraq, IPC ceased its operations after it was nationalised by the <a href="/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq" title="Ba&#39;athist Iraq">Ba'athist Iraqi</a> government in June 1972 although legally Iraq Petroleum Company still remains in existence,<sup id="cite_ref-cc_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cc-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and one of its associated companies —<a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_Petroleum_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu Dhabi Petroleum Company">Abu Dhabi Petroleum Company</a> (ADPC), formerly Petroleum Development (Trucial Coast) Ltd — also continues with the original shareholding intact.<sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2012-100_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2012-100-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2012-101_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2012-101-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The intensified power struggle between oil companies and host governments in Middle East, along with the oil price shocks that followed the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a> meant British Petroleum lost most of its direct access to crude oil supplies produced in countries that belonged to the Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries (<a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>), and prompted it to diversify its operations beyond the heavily Middle East dependent oil production. In 1976, BP and Shell de-merged their marketing operations in the United Kingdom by dividing Shell-Mex and BP. In 1978, the company acquired a controlling interest in <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_Ohio" title="Standard Oil of Ohio">Standard Oil of Ohio</a> (Sohio).<sup id="cite_ref-NYtimes_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYtimes-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Iran, British Petroleum continued to operate until the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Islamic Revolution</a> in 1979. The new regime of <a href="/wiki/Ayatollah_Khomeini" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayatollah Khomeini">Ayatollah Khomeini</a> nationalised all of the company's assets in Iran without compensation, bringing to an end its 70-year presence in Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As a result, BP lost 40% of its global crude oil supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt200379_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt200379-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1970–1980s BP diversified into <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minerals" class="mw-redirect" title="Minerals">minerals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nutrition" title="Nutrition">nutrition</a> businesses which all were divested later.<sup id="cite_ref-beale_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beale-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1979_to_1997">1979 to 1997</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1979 to 1997">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_old_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/BP_old_logo.svg/220px-BP_old_logo.svg.png" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/BP_old_logo.svg/330px-BP_old_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/BP_old_logo.svg/440px-BP_old_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="304" data-file-height="288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_old_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The final version of the BP shield logo, introduced in 1989 and used until 2000; the shield logo was originally designed by AR Saunders in 1920</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">British government</a> sold 80&#160;million shares of BP at $7.58 in 1979 as part of <a href="/wiki/Premiership_of_Margaret_Thatcher" title="Premiership of Margaret Thatcher">Thatcher-era</a> privatisation. This sale represented slightly more than 5% of BP's total shares and reduced the government's ownership of the company to 46%.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe1979_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe1979-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>  After the worldwide stock market crash on 19 October 1987, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> initiated the sale of an additional GBP7.5 billion ($12.2 billion) of BP shares at 333 pence, representing the government's remaining 31% stake in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Lohr1987_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lohr1987-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 1987 the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Investment_Authority" title="Kuwait Investment Authority">Kuwait Investment Office</a> purchased a 10.06% interest in BP, becoming the largest institutional shareholder.<sup id="cite_ref-TorontoStar1987_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TorontoStar1987-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>  The following May, the KIO purchased additional shares, bringing their ownership to 21.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt191187_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt191187-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> This raised concerns within BP that operations in the United States, BP's primary country of operations, would suffer. In October 1988, the British <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Trade_and_Industry_(United_Kingdom)" title="Department of Trade and Industry (United Kingdom)">Department of Trade and Industry</a> required the KIO to reduce its shares to 9.6% within 12 months.<sup id="cite_ref-OConnor1988_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OConnor1988-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Peter_Walters" title="Peter Walters">Peter Walters</a> was the company chairman from 1981 to 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-lat080989_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat080989-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>  During his period as chairman he reduced company's refining capacity in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-lat080989_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat080989-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>  In 1982, the <a href="/wiki/Downstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Downstream (petroleum industry)">downstream</a> assets of BP Canada were sold to <a href="/wiki/Petro_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Petro Canada">Petro Canada</a>. In 1984, <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Oil of California">Standard Oil of California</a> was renamed to <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron Corporation</a>; and it bought Gulf Oil—the largest merger in history at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-CVX-H-01_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CVX-H-01-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>  To meet anti-trust regulations, Chevron divested many of Gulf's operating subsidiaries, and sold some Gulf stations and a refinery in the eastern United States to British Petroleum and <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Farms" title="Cumberland Farms">Cumberland Farms</a> in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-chevron-profile_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chevron-profile-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>  In 1987, British Petroleum negotiated the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Britoil" title="Britoil">Britoil</a><sup id="cite_ref-ap050288_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap050288-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and the remaining publicly traded shares of Standard Oil of Ohio.<sup id="cite_ref-NYtimes_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYtimes-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>  At the same year it was listed on the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Stock_Exchange" title="Tokyo Stock Exchange">Tokyo Stock Exchange</a> where its share were traded until delisting in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters240608_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters240608-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Walters was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Horton_(businessman)" title="Robert Horton (businessman)">Robert Horton</a> in 1990. Horton carried out a major corporate down-sizing exercise removing various tiers of management at the Head Office.<sup id="cite_ref-roberts_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roberts-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>  In 1992, British Petroleum sold off its 57% stake in BP Canada (<a href="/wiki/Upstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Upstream (petroleum industry)">upstream</a> operations), which was renamed as <a href="/wiki/Talisman_Energy" title="Talisman Energy">Talisman Energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TLM-H-01_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TLM-H-01-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Browne,_Baron_Browne_of_Madingley" title="John Browne, Baron Browne of Madingley">John Browne</a>, who had joined BP in 1966 and rose through the ranks to join the board as managing director in 1991, was appointed group chief executive in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-browne_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-browne-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1981, British Petroleum entered into the solar technology sector by acquiring 50% of Lucas Energy Systems, a company which became Lucas BP Solar Systems, and later <a href="/wiki/BP_Solar" title="BP Solar">BP Solar</a>. The company was a manufacturer and installer of <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> <a href="/wiki/Solar_cells" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar cells">solar cells</a>. It became wholly owned by British Petroleum in the mid-1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>British Petroleum entered into Russian market in 1990 and opened its first service station in Moscow in 1996. In 1997, it acquired 10% stake in Russian oil company <a href="/wiki/Sidanco" class="mw-redirect" title="Sidanco">Sidanco</a>, which later became a part of TNK-BP.<sup id="cite_ref-mt290212_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mt290212-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1992, the company entered into Azerbaijani market. In 1994, it signed the production sharing agreement for the <a href="/wiki/Azeri%E2%80%93Chirag%E2%80%93Guneshli" class="mw-redirect" title="Azeri–Chirag–Guneshli">Azeri–Chirag–Guneshli</a> oil project and in 1995 for the <a href="/wiki/Shah_Deniz_gas_field" title="Shah Deniz gas field">Shah Deniz gas field</a> development.<sup id="cite_ref-caspia_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caspia-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1998_to_2009">1998 to 2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1998 to 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under John Browne, British Petroleum acquired other oil companies, transforming BP into the third largest oil company in the world. British Petroleum merged with <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a> (formerly Standard Oil of Indiana) in December 1998, becoming BP Amoco plc.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc110899_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc110899-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-namechg_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-namechg-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Most Amoco stations in the United States were converted to BP's brand and corporate identity. In 2000, BP Amoco acquired <a href="/wiki/ARCO" title="ARCO">Arco (Atlantic Richfield Co.)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burmah_Oil" title="Burmah Oil">Burmah Castrol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bp140300_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bp140300-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brierley_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brierley-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCNews2000_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNews2000-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  As part of the merger's brand awareness, the company helped the <a href="/wiki/Tate_Modern" title="Tate Modern">Tate Modern</a> gallery of British Art launch <i>RePresenting Britain 1500–2000</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-observer190300_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observer190300-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>  In 2001, in response to negative press on British Petroleum's poor safety standards, the company adopted a green <a href="/wiki/Sunburst" title="Sunburst">sunburst</a> logo and rebranded itself as BP ("Beyond Petroleum") plc.<sup id="cite_ref-namechg_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-namechg-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg/220px-Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg/330px-Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg/440px-Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="1168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steven_Koonin_BP_2005-02-22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Steven Koonin, BP's then-Chief Scientist, speaking in the company boardroom in 2005 (top right of picture)</div></div></div>
<p>In the beginning of the 2000s, BP became the leading partner (and later operator) of the <a href="/wiki/Baku%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Ceyhan_pipeline" title="Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline">Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline</a> project which opened a new oil transportation route from the Caspian region.<sup id="cite_ref-ft260505_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft260505-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>  In 2002, BP acquired the majority of Veba Öl AG, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/VEBA_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="VEBA AG">VEBA AG</a>, and subsequently rebranded its existing stations in Germany to the Aral name.<sup id="cite_ref-BPAral_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPAral-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>  As part of the deal, BP acquired also the Veba Öl's stake in Ruhr Öl joint venture. Ruhr Öl was dissolved in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 September 2003, BP and a group of Russian billionaires, known as AAR (<a href="/wiki/Alfa_Group" title="Alfa Group">Alfa</a>-<a href="/wiki/Access_Industries" title="Access Industries">Access</a>-<a href="/wiki/Renova_Group" title="Renova Group">Renova</a>), announced the creation of a strategic partnership to jointly hold their oil assets in Russia and Ukraine. As a result, TNK-ВР was created.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn260603_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn260603-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, BP's <a href="/wiki/Olefins" class="mw-redirect" title="Olefins">olefins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Derivative_(chemistry)" title="Derivative (chemistry)">derivatives</a> business was moved into a separate entity which was sold to <a href="/wiki/Ineos" title="Ineos">Ineos</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc071005_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc071005-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bp161205_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bp161205-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>  In 2007, BP sold its corporate-owned convenience stores, typically known as "<a href="/wiki/BP_Connect" class="mw-redirect" title="BP Connect">BP Connect</a>", to local <a href="/wiki/Franchisee" class="mw-redirect" title="Franchisee">franchisees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jobber_(fuel)" title="Jobber (fuel)">jobbers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bp151107_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bp151107-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 March 2005, 15 workers were killed and more than 170 injured in the <a href="/wiki/Texas_City_Refinery_explosion" title="Texas City Refinery explosion">Texas City Refinery explosion</a>. To save money, major upgrades to the 1934 refinery had been postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>  Browne pledged to prevent another catastrophe. Three months later, '<a href="/wiki/Thunder_Horse_PDQ" title="Thunder Horse PDQ">Thunder Horse PDQ</a>', BP's giant new production platform in the Gulf of Mexico, nearly sank during a hurricane. In their rush to finish the $1 billion platform, workers had installed a valve backwards, allowing the ballast tanks to flood. Inspections revealed other shoddy work. Repairs costing hundreds of millions would keep Thunder Horse out of commission for three years.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lord Browne resigned from BP on 1 May 2007. The head of exploration and production <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hayward" title="Tony Hayward">Tony Hayward</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian020507_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian020507-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> became the new chief executive.  In 2009, Hayward shifted emphasis from Lord Browne's focus on alternative energy, announcing that safety would henceforth be the company's "number one priority".<sup id="cite_ref-bbc110509_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc110509-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, BP formed with <a href="/wiki/AB_Sugar" class="mw-redirect" title="AB Sugar">AB Sugar</a> and <a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">DuPont</a> a joint venture Vivergo Fuels which opened a bioethanol plant in <a href="/wiki/Salt_End" title="Salt End">Saltend</a> near <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, United Kingdom in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters061212_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters061212-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Together with DuPont, BP formed a <a href="/wiki/Biobutanol" class="mw-redirect" title="Biobutanol">biobutanol</a> joint venture Butamax by acquiring biobutan technology company Biobutanol LLC in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters080709_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters080709-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, BP obtained a production contract during the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Iraq#2009_Oil_services_contracts" title="Economy of Iraq">2009/2010 Iraqi oil services contracts tender</a> to develop the <a href="/wiki/Rumaila_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Rumaila field">Rumaila field</a> with joint venture partner <a href="/wiki/CNPC" class="mw-redirect" title="CNPC">CNPC</a>, which contain an estimated 17 billion barrels (2.7<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil, accounting for 12% of Iraq's oil reserves estimated at 143.1 billion barrels (22.75<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>9</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2012-83_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2012-83-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2010-66_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2010-66-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In June 2010, the BP/CNPC consortium took over development of the field,<sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2009-53_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2009-53-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-2009-53-B_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-2009-53-B-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> which was the epicentre of the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Gulf_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf war">Gulf war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-1990-01_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-1990-01-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GT-DEX-1990-02_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GT-DEX-1990-02-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_to_present">2010 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2010 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama-hayward.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Obama-hayward.jpg/220px-Obama-hayward.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Obama-hayward.jpg/330px-Obama-hayward.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Obama-hayward.jpg/440px-Obama-hayward.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama-hayward.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Barack Obama meeting with BP executives at the White House in June 2010 to discuss the oil spill in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_Connect_Kapiti,_New_Zealand.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/BP_Connect_Kapiti%2C_New_Zealand.jpg/220px-BP_Connect_Kapiti%2C_New_Zealand.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/BP_Connect_Kapiti%2C_New_Zealand.jpg/330px-BP_Connect_Kapiti%2C_New_Zealand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/BP_Connect_Kapiti%2C_New_Zealand.jpg/440px-BP_Connect_Kapiti%2C_New_Zealand.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1449" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_Connect_Kapiti,_New_Zealand.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A modern BP filling station on the <a href="/wiki/Kapiti_Coast" title="Kapiti Coast">Kapiti Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> with Wild Bean Cafe and BP Connect, shop built in late 2015</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_filling_station,_Pudsey_Road_(geograph_4680793).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BP_filling_station%2C_Pudsey_Road_%28geograph_4680793%29.jpg/220px-BP_filling_station%2C_Pudsey_Road_%28geograph_4680793%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BP_filling_station%2C_Pudsey_Road_%28geograph_4680793%29.jpg/330px-BP_filling_station%2C_Pudsey_Road_%28geograph_4680793%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BP_filling_station%2C_Pudsey_Road_%28geograph_4680793%29.jpg/440px-BP_filling_station%2C_Pudsey_Road_%28geograph_4680793%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_filling_station,_Pudsey_Road_(geograph_4680793).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A modern BP filling station in <a href="/wiki/Bramley,_Leeds" title="Bramley, Leeds">Bramley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>On 1 October 2010, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dudley" title="Bob Dudley">Bob Dudley</a> replaced <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hayward" title="Tony Hayward">Tony Hayward</a> as the company's CEO after the Deepwater Horizon oil spill.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters300910_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters300910-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> After the oil spill BP announced a divestment program to sell about $38 billion worth of non-core assets by 2013 to compensate its liabilities related to the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj100912_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj100912-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nasdaq_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasdaq-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In July 2010, it sold its natural gas activities in <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, Canada, to <a href="/wiki/Apache_Corporation" title="Apache Corporation">Apache Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fp300712_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp300712-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> It sold its stake in the Petroperijá and Boquerón fields in Venezuela and in the Lan Tay and Lan Do fields, the Nam Con Son pipeline and terminal, and the <a href="/wiki/Phu_My_3_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Phu My 3 power plant">Phu My 3 power plant</a> in Vietnam to TNK-BP,<sup id="cite_ref-reuters271010_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters271010-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg181010_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg181010-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Forecourt" title="Forecourt">forecourts</a> and supply businesses in Namibia, Botswana, Zambia, Tanzania and Malawi to <a href="/wiki/Puma_Energy" title="Puma Energy">Puma Energy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-reuters151110_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters151110-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Wytch_Farm" title="Wytch Farm">Wytch Farm</a> onshore oilfield in <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a> and a package of North Sea gas assets to <a href="/wiki/Perenco" title="Perenco">Perenco</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wsj270312_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj270312-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> natural-gas liquids business in Canada to <a href="/wiki/Plains_All_American_Pipeline_LP" class="mw-redirect" title="Plains All American Pipeline LP">Plains All American Pipeline LP</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg011211_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg011211-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> natural gas assets in Kansas to <a href="/wiki/Linn_Energy" title="Linn Energy">Linn Energy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wichita280212_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wichita280212-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Carson Refinery in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a> and its ARCO retail network to <a href="/wiki/Tesoro" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesoro">Tesoro</a>, Sunray and Hemphill gas processing plants in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, together with their associated gas gathering system, to Eagle Rock Energy Partners,<sup id="cite_ref-ft180912_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft180912-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CarsonSale_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CarsonSale-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bp100812_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bp100812-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> the Texas City Refinery and associated assets to <a href="/wiki/Marathon_Petroleum" title="Marathon Petroleum">Marathon Petroleum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-reuters081012_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters081012-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-biz010213_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biz010213-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> located Marlin, Dorado, King, Horn Mountain, and Holstein fields as also its stake in non-operated Diana Hoover and Ram Powell fields to <a href="/wiki/Plains_Exploration_%26_Production" title="Plains Exploration &amp; Production">Plains Exploration &amp; Production</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wsj100912_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj100912-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> non-operating stake in the <a href="/wiki/Draugen_oil_field" title="Draugen oil field">Draugen oil field</a> to <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Norske Shell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-reuters130912_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters130912-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and the UK's liquefied petroleum gas distribution business to DCC.<sup id="cite_ref-be090812_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-be090812-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2011, BP formed a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Reliance_Industries" title="Reliance Industries">Reliance Industries</a>, taking a 30% stake in a new Indian joint-venture for an initial payment of $7.2&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In September 2012, BP sold its subsidiary BP Chemicals (Malaysia) Sdn. Bhd., an operator of the Kuantan <a href="/wiki/Purified_terephthalic_acid" class="mw-redirect" title="Purified terephthalic acid">purified terephthalic acid</a> (PTA) plant in Malaysia, to Reliance Industries for $230 million.<sup id="cite_ref-bl290912_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl290912-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>  In October 2012, BP sold its stake in TNK-BP to Rosneft for $12.3&#160;billion in cash and 18.5% of Rosneft's stock.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters221012_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters221012-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The deal was completed on 21 March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters220313_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters220313-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>  In 2012, BP acquired an acreage in the <a href="/wiki/Utica_Shale" title="Utica Shale">Utica Shale</a> but these developments plans were cancelled in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-platts29042014_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-platts29042014-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011–2015, BP cut down its alternative energy business. The company announced its departure from the solar energy market in December 2011 by closing its solar power business, BP Solar.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters211211_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters211211-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, BP shut down the <a href="/wiki/BP_Biofuels_Highlands" title="BP Biofuels Highlands">BP Biofuels Highlands</a> project which was developed since 2008 to make <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">cellulosic ethanol</a> from emerging energy crops like <a href="/wiki/Switchgrass" class="mw-redirect" title="Switchgrass">switchgrass</a> and from <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sunshine_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunshine-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bfd261012_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bfd261012-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>  In 2015, BP decided to exit from other <a href="/wiki/Lignocellulosic_ethanol" class="mw-redirect" title="Lignocellulosic ethanol">lignocellulosic ethanol</a> businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-bfd180115_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bfd180115-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>  It sold its stake in Vivergo to <a href="/wiki/Associated_British_Foods" title="Associated British Foods">Associated British Foods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-farmersweekly080515_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-farmersweekly080515-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>  BP and DuPont also mothballed their joint biobutanol pilot plant in Saltend.<sup id="cite_ref-bfd171215_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bfd171215-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2014, BP agreed to a deal worth around $20 billion to supply <a href="/wiki/CNOOC" class="mw-redirect" title="CNOOC">CNOOC</a> with liquefied natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters17062014_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters17062014-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Statoil_Fuel_%26_Retail" title="Statoil Fuel &amp; Retail">Statoil Fuel &amp; Retail</a> sold its aviation fuel business to BP.  To ensure the approval of competition authorities, BP agreed to sell the former Statoil aviation fuel businesses in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport" title="Stockholm Arlanda Airport">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_Landvetter_Airport" title="Göteborg Landvetter Airport">Gothenburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6_Airport" title="Malmö Airport">Malmö</a> airports to <a href="/wiki/World_Fuel_Services" title="World Fuel Services">World Fuel Services</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-ain19082015_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ain19082015-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, BP sold its <a href="/wiki/Decatur,_Alabama" title="Decatur, Alabama">Decatur, Alabama</a>, plant to <a href="/wiki/Indorama_Ventures" title="Indorama Ventures">Indorama Ventures</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Blum16_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blum16-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> At the same year, its Norwegian daughter company BP Norge merged with Det Norske Oljeselskap to form <a href="/wiki/Aker_BP" title="Aker BP">Aker BP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rigzone300916_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rigzone300916-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2017, the company reached an agreement to sell its <a href="/wiki/Forties_pipeline_system" title="Forties pipeline system">Forties pipeline system</a> in the North Sea to <a href="/wiki/Ineos" title="Ineos">Ineos</a> for $250 million. The sale included terminals at <a href="/wiki/Dalmeny" title="Dalmeny">Dalmeny</a> and Kinneil, a site in Aberdeen, and the Forties Unity Platform.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the company floated its subsidiary BP Midstream Partners LP, a pipeline operator in the United States, at the New York Stock Exchange. In Argentina, BP and <a href="/wiki/Bridas_Corporation" title="Bridas Corporation">Bridas Corporation</a> agreed to merge their interests in Pan American Energy and Axion Energy to form a jointly owned Pan American Energy Group.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters110917_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters110917-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, BP announced a planned investment of $200&#160;million to acquire a 43% stake in the solar energy developer <a href="/wiki/Lightsource_Renewable_Energy" title="Lightsource Renewable Energy">Lightsource Renewable Energy</a>, a company which will be renamed Lightsource BP.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg151217_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg151217-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In March 2017, the company acquired Clean Energy's biomethane business and assets, including its production sites and existing supply contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-Hardcastle17_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hardcastle17-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In April 2017, its subsidiary Butamax bought an <a href="/wiki/Isobutanol" title="Isobutanol">isobutanol</a> production company Nesika Energy.<sup id="cite_ref-biomass030417_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biomass030417-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2018, the company agreed to purchase its shale assets from Australian mining and petroleum conglomerate <a href="/wiki/BHP" title="BHP">BHP</a> for $10.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BPheadoffice.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BPheadoffice.JPG/220px-BPheadoffice.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BPheadoffice.JPG/330px-BPheadoffice.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BPheadoffice.JPG/440px-BPheadoffice.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BPheadoffice.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BP's world headquarters in <a href="/wiki/St._James%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="St. James&#39;s">St. James's</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>, London</div></div></div>
<p>BP has operations in approximately 70&#160;countries worldwide<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-glance_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-glance-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> with the global headquarters in London, United Kingdom. BP operations are organized into two main business segments, <a href="/wiki/Upstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Upstream (petroleum industry)">Upstream</a> and <a href="/wiki/Downstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Downstream (petroleum industry)">Downstream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-segments_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-segments-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1951, BP has annually published its <i>Statistical Review of <a href="/wiki/World_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="World Energy">World Energy</a></i>, which is considered an energy industry benchmark.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters120613_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters120613-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations_by_location">Operations by location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operations by location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg/220px-Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg/330px-Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg/440px-Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hedon_Clough_and_the_BP_Chemicals_site_at_Saltend_-_geograph.org.uk_-_145508.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The BP chemicals plant in <a href="/wiki/Salt_End" title="Salt End">Saltend</a> near <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, United Kingdom</div></div></div>
<p>BP has a major corporate campus in <a href="/wiki/Sunbury-on-Thames" title="Sunbury-on-Thames">Sunbury-on-Thames</a> which is home to around 3,500&#160;employees and over 50&#160;business units.<sup id="cite_ref-BP-Sunbury_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP-Sunbury-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> operations are headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.  BP's trading functions are based at <a href="/wiki/20_Canada_Square" title="20 Canada Square">20 Canada Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf" title="Canary Wharf">Canary Wharf</a>, London.  BP has three major research and development centres in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-commons2012_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commons2012-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP operates more than 40&#160;offshore oil and gas fields, four onshore terminals and a pipeline network that transports around 50%t of the oil and gas produced in the UK, according to the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Wachman_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wachman-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> BP has invested more than £35 billion in the North Sea since the 1960s, and in 2012 announced its plans to invest another £10&#160;billion until 2017.  The company announced that it is focusing its investment in the UK North Sea into four development projects including the <a href="/wiki/Clair_oilfield" title="Clair oilfield">Clair</a>, Devenick, <a href="/wiki/Schiehallion_oilfield" title="Schiehallion oilfield">Schiehallion and Loyal</a>, and Kinnoull oilfields.<sup id="cite_ref-Swint2011_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swint2011-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>  BP is the operator of the Clair oilfield, which has been appraised as the largest hydrocarbon resource in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Bawden2011_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bawden2011-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Saltend near Hull, BP operates a petrochemicals plant that produces <a href="/wiki/Acetic_acid" title="Acetic acid">acetic acid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acetic_anhydride" title="Acetic anhydride">acetic anhydride</a> used in the production of pharmaceuticals, textiles and other chemical products.<sup id="cite_ref-BPUK_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPUK-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ICIS2007_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICIS2007-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are 1,200&#160;BP service stations in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Gosden16_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gosden16-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BP-UK_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP-UK-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BPAmericasHQ.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BPAmericasHQ.JPG/220px-BPAmericasHQ.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BPAmericasHQ.JPG/330px-BPAmericasHQ.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BPAmericasHQ.JPG/440px-BPAmericasHQ.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BPAmericasHQ.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The headquarters of BP America in <a href="/wiki/Westlake_Park_(Houston)" title="Westlake Park (Houston)">Westlake Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg/220px-Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg/330px-Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg/440px-Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1682" data-file-height="1260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thunder_Horse_Semisub.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Thunder_Horse_PDQ" title="Thunder Horse PDQ">Thunder Horse PDQ</a></i> semi-submersible oil platform in the <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Horse_Oil_Field" title="Thunder Horse Oil Field">Thunder Horse Oil Field</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg/220px-Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg/330px-Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg/440px-Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Part of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System" title="Trans-Alaska Pipeline System">Trans-Alaska Pipeline System</a></div></div></div>
<p>The United States operations comprise nearly one-third of BP's worldwide business interests,<sup id="cite_ref-NYTBusiness2012_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTBusiness2012-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> and the United States is the country with the greatest concentration of its employees and investments.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPUS_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPUS-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>  BP employs approximately 14,000&#160;people in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-BPUnitedStates_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPUnitedStates-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, BP's total production in the United States included 370,000 barrels per day (59,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of oil and 1.659&#160;billion cubic feet per day (47.0&#160;million cubic metres per day) of natural gas<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-production_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-production-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> and its refinery throughput was 713,000 barrels per day (113,400&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d).<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-refining_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-refining-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
