</p><p>BP's major subsidiary in the United States is BP America, Inc. based in <a href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston, Texas">Houston, Texas</a>, which is the parent company for the BP's operations in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-biz030513_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biz030513-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>  BP Exploration &amp; Production Inc., a 1996 established Houston-based subsidiary, is dealing with oil exploration and production, including Gulf of Mexico activities.<sup id="cite_ref-bpexploration_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpexploration-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> BP Corporation North America, Inc., provides petroleum refining services as also transportation fuel, heat and light energy, and petrochemical products.<sup id="cite_ref-bpcorporation_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpcorporation-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> BP Products North America, Inc., a 1954 established Houston-based subsidiary, is engaged in the exploration, development, production, refining, and marketing of oil and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-bpproduct_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpproduct-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> BP America Production Company, a <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>-based subsidiary, engages in oil and gas exploration and development.<sup id="cite_ref-bpproduction_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpproduction-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> BP Energy Company, a Houston-based subsidiary, is a provider of natural gas, power, and risk management services to the industrial and utility sectors and a retail electric provider in Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-bpenergy_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpenergy-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP's upstream activities are divided into three business areas which are deepwater Gulf of Mexico, the Lower 48&#160;states, and Alaska.  BP is a leading acreage holder and producer of oil and natural gas in the deepwater <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reed2014a_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reed2014a-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the company produces about 300,000 barrels per day (48,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of oil equivalent in the Gulf of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-Crooks17_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crooks17-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> BP operates the <a href="/wiki/Atlantis_oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantis oil field">Atlantis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mad_Dog_oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Mad Dog oil field">Mad Dog</a>, Na Kika, and <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Horse_oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Thunder Horse oil field">Thunder Horse</a> production platforms while holding interest in hubs operated by other companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Ambrose17_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ambrose17-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BP-Gulf_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP-Gulf-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the company operated nine North Slope oilfields in the Greater Prudhoe Bay area, producing 107,900 barrels per day (17,150&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d).<sup id="cite_ref-AR16-upstream-regions_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR16-upstream-regions-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>  BP is the largest partner with just under 50% ownership stake in the 800-mile (1,300&#160;km) long <a href="/wiki/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System" title="Trans-Alaska Pipeline System">Trans-Alaska Pipeline System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-miner311012_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miner311012-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, BP moved its onshore unit in the United States to a new business called U.S. Lower 48 Onshore to compete in the burgeoning shale gas industry dominated by smaller companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Eaton16_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eaton16-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>  It has a 7.5 billion barrels (1.19&#160;billion cubic metres) material resource base on 5.7&#160;million acres (23,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-OGJ15_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OGJ15-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>  It has <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas_in_the_United_States" title="Shale gas in the United States">shale positions</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas_in_the_United_States#Woodford_Shale,_Oklahoma" title="Shale gas in the United States">Woodford, Oklahoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas_in_the_United_States#Fayetteville_Shale,_Arkansas" title="Shale gas in the United States">Fayetteville, Arkansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas_in_the_United_States#Haynesville_Shale,_Louisiana" title="Shale gas in the United States">Haynesville, Texas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eagle_Ford_Formation" class="mw-redirect" title="Eagle Ford Formation">Eagle Ford, Texas</a> shales.<sup id="cite_ref-Pulsinelli2014_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pulsinelli2014-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rouan2012_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rouan2012-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>  It has <a href="/wiki/Unconventional_gas" title="Unconventional gas">unconventional gas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Shale_gas" title="Shale gas">shale gas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tight_gas" title="Tight gas">tight gas</a>) stakes also in Colorado, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> and Wyoming, primarily in the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Basin" title="San Juan Basin">San Juan Basin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hasterok2012_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hasterok2012-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ZacksJun2012_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZacksJun2012-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPUSExploration_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPUSExploration-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP operates <a href="/wiki/Whiting_Refinery" title="Whiting Refinery">Whiting Refinery</a> in Indiana,<sup id="cite_ref-BPUSRefining_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPUSRefining-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Point_Refinery" title="Cherry Point Refinery">Cherry Point Refinery</a> in Washington,<sup id="cite_ref-BPUSRefining_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPUSRefining-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo_Refinery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Toledo Refinery (page does not exist)">Toledo Refinery</a> in Ohio, which is owned by BP and <a href="/wiki/Husky_Energy" title="Husky Energy">Husky Energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BPUSRefining_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPUSRefining-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReutersUK2012_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersUK2012-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Blade2012_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blade2012-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company owns two petrochemical plants in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-Blum16_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blum16-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPPetrochemicals_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPPetrochemicals-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>  Its petrochemical plant in Texas City, located on the same site as the formerly owned Texas City Refinery, produces industrial chemicals including <a href="/wiki/Propene" title="Propene">propylene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Styrene" title="Styrene">styrene</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sixel2005_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sixel2005-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> BP's Cooper River, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> petrochemical plant produces PTA, which is used in the production of <a href="/wiki/Polyester" title="Polyester">synthetic fibre</a> for clothing, packaging and <a href="/wiki/Thin-film_optics" title="Thin-film optics">optical films</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ICIS150617_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICIS150617-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  May&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, BP operated 13&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wind_farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind farms">wind farms</a> in seven states in the U.S., and held an interest in another in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BP-wind_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP-wind-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the company generated  4.389&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour#Multiples" title="Kilowatt hour">TW·h</a> of wind power.<sup id="cite_ref-AR16-wind_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR16-wind-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_locations">Other locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Egypt, BP produces approximately 15% of the country's total oil production and 40% of its domestic gas.<sup id="cite_ref-Petzet2012_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petzet2012-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The company also has offshore gas developments in the East Nile Delta Mediterranean, and in the West Nile Delta,<sup id="cite_ref-ZacksJune2012_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZacksJune2012-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> where the company has a joint investment of US$9&#160;billion with <a href="/wiki/RWE" title="RWE">RWE</a> to develop two offshore gas fields.<sup id="cite_ref-Hromadko2010_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hromadko2010-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPWestNile2010_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPWestNile2010-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP is active in offshore oil development in Angola, where it holds an interest in a total of nine oil exploration and production blocks covering more than 30,000 square kilometres (12,000&#160;sq&#160;mi). This includes four blocks it acquired in December 2011 and an additional block that is operated by Brazilian national oil company, <a href="/wiki/Petrobras" title="Petrobras">Petrobras</a>, in which it holds a 40% stake.<sup id="cite_ref-BPAngolaAcquisition_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPAngolaAcquisition-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP has a stake in exploration of two blocks of offshore deepwater assets in the South China Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-China2012_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China2012-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xu2012_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xu2012-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In India, BP owns a 30% share of oil and gas assets operated by <a href="/wiki/Reliance_Industries" title="Reliance Industries">Reliance Industries</a>, including exploration and production rights in more than 20&#160;offshore oil and gas blocks, representing an investment of more than US$7&#160;billion into oil and gas exploration in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Sharma2011_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma2011-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP has major liquefied natural gas activities in Indonesia, where it operates the <a href="/wiki/Tangguh_gas_field" title="Tangguh gas field">Tangguh LNG</a> project, which began production in 2009 and has a capacity of 7.6&#160;million tonnes of liquid natural gas per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Grieder2009_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grieder2009-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Also in that country, the company has invested in the exploration and development of <a href="/wiki/Coalbed_methane" title="Coalbed methane">coalbed methane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Suhana2011_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suhana2011-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP operates in Iraq as part of the joint venture <a href="/wiki/Rumaila_Field_Operating_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Rumaila Field Operating Organization">Rumaila Operating Organization</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Rumaila_oil_field" title="Rumaila oil field">Rumaila oil field</a>, the world's fourth largest oilfield, where it produced over 1 million barrels per day (160<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>3</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of oil equivalent in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersOct2009_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersOct2009-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UPIJan11_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPIJan11-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Road_Train2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Road_Train2.jpg/220px-Road_Train2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Road_Train2.jpg/330px-Road_Train2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Road_Train2.jpg/440px-Road_Train2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Road_Train2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A BP <a href="/wiki/Road_train" title="Road train">road train</a> in the Australian outback</div></div></div>
<p>BP operates the <a href="/wiki/Kwinana_Oil_Refinery" title="Kwinana Oil Refinery">Kwinana</a> refinery in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>, which can process up to 146,000 barrels per day (23,200&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of crude oil and is the country's largest refinery,<sup id="cite_ref-Denton15_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denton15-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> supplying fuel to 80%t of Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight17_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight17-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>  BP is a non-operating joint venture partner in the <a href="/wiki/North_West_Shelf" title="North West Shelf">North West Shelf</a>, which produces LNG, pipeline gas, condensate and oil.<sup id="cite_ref-Chambers16_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chambers16-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The NWS venture is Australia's largest resource development and accounts for around one third of Australia's oil and gas production.<sup id="cite_ref-Lanis17_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lanis17-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Daiss16_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daiss16-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP operates the two largest oil and gas production projects in the Azerbaijan's sector of the Caspian Sea, the <a href="/wiki/Azeri%E2%80%93Chirag%E2%80%93Guneshli" class="mw-redirect" title="Azeri–Chirag–Guneshli">Azeri–Chirag–Guneshli</a> offshore oil fields, which supplies 80% of the country's oil production, and the <a href="/wiki/Shah_Deniz_gas_field" title="Shah Deniz gas field">Shah Deniz gas field</a>. It also and develops the <a href="/wiki/Shafag-Asiman" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafag-Asiman">Shafag-Asiman</a> complex of offshore geological structures.<sup id="cite_ref-Neff2010_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neff2010-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yevgrashina2012_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yevgrashina2012-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-today_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-today-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> In addition, it operates the <a href="/wiki/Sangachal_Terminal" title="Sangachal Terminal">Sangachal terminal</a> and the Azerbaijan's major export pipelines through <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Baku%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Ceyhan_pipeline" title="Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline">Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baku%E2%80%93Supsa_Pipeline" title="Baku–Supsa Pipeline">Baku–Supsa</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus_Pipeline" title="South Caucasus Pipeline">South Caucasus</a> pipelines.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_depot,_Frontignan,_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Oil_depot%2C_Frontignan%2C_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg/220px-Oil_depot%2C_Frontignan%2C_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Oil_depot%2C_Frontignan%2C_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg/330px-Oil_depot%2C_Frontignan%2C_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Oil_depot%2C_Frontignan%2C_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg/440px-Oil_depot%2C_Frontignan%2C_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4882" data-file-height="3051" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_depot,_Frontignan,_H%C3%A9rault_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A GDH (subsidiary of BP) oil depot, Frontigan, Hérault, France.</div></div></div>
<p>BP's refining operations in continental Europe include Europe's second-largest oil refinery, located in Rotterdam, the Netherlands, which can process up to 377,000 barrels (59,900&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of crude oil per day.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters2009_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters2009-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to its offshore operations in the British zone of North Sea, BP has interests in the Norwegian section of the sea through its stake in Aker BP.  As of  December&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, BP holds a 19.75% stake in Russia's state-controlled oil company Rosneft.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters220313_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters220313-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AR17-Rosneft_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-Rosneft-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP's Canadian operations are headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a> and the company operates primarily in <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>. It purchases crude oil for the company's refineries in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, has <a href="/wiki/Oil_sand" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil sand">oil sands</a> holdings in <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> and four offshore blocks in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BPCanada_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPCanada-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPCanadianOilSands_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPCanadianOilSands-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-upstream1611112_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream1611112-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>  The company's <a href="/wiki/Athabasca_oil_sands" title="Athabasca oil sands">Canadian oil sands</a> leases include joint ventures with <a href="/wiki/Husky_Energy" title="Husky Energy">Husky Energy</a> in the Sunrise Energy Project (50%),<sup id="cite_ref-Watkins2010_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watkins2010-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Devon_Energy" title="Devon Energy">Devon Energy</a> in Pike,<sup id="cite_ref-DevonEnergy2010_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DevonEnergy2010-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> and a partnership with Value Creation Inc. in the development of the Terre de Grace oil sands lease. The BP's investment in the Sunrise Project is £1.6&#160;billion and it is expected to start production in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> In May 2017, it was reported that BP is considering to sell-off its oil sands assets.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters200417_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters200417-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP is the largest oil and gas producer in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, where it holds more than 1,350 square kilometres (520&#160;sq&#160;mi) of offshore assets and is the largest shareholder in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_LNG" title="Atlantic LNG">Atlantic LNG</a>, one of the largest <a href="/wiki/LNG_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="LNG plant">LNG plants</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UPIMay11_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPIMay11-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Brazil, BP holds stakes in offshore oil and gas exploration in the Barreirinhas, Ceará and <a href="/wiki/Campos_Basin" title="Campos Basin">Campos</a> basins, in addition to onshore processing facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Flynn2012_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flynn2012-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> BP also operates biofuel production facilities in Brazil, including three cane sugar mills for ethanol production.<sup id="cite_ref-Fick2011_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fick2011-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AFReutersSep11_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFReutersSep11-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration_and_production">Exploration and production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Exploration and production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Oil_fields_operated_by_BP" title="Oil fields operated by BP">Oil fields operated by BP</a></div>
<p>BP upstream's activities include exploring for new oil and natural gas resources, developing access to such resources, and producing, transporting, storing and processing oil and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2012_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2012-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNNMoney2011_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNMoney2011-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The activities in this area of operations take place in 29&#160;countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-upstream_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-upstream-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, BP produced around 3.6 million barrels per day (570<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>3</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of oil equivalent,<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-glance_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-glance-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> of which  2.26 million barrels per day (359<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>3</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) were liquids and 7.744&#160;billion cubic feet (219.3&#160;million cubic metres) was natural gas,<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-performance24_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-performance24-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> and had total proved reserves of 18.441 million barrels per day (2.9319<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of oil equivalent,<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-glance_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-glance-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> of which liquids accounted 10.672 million barrels per day (1.6967<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d)<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-provenreserves_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-provenreserves-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> and natural gas 45.06&#160;trillion cubic feet (1.276&#160;trillion cubic metres)<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-provenreserves_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-provenreserves-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the conventional oil exploration and production, BP has a stake in the three oil sands projects in Canada although it is considering to sell its oil sands assets.<sup id="cite_ref-fp300712_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp300712-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters200417_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters200417-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refining_and_marketing">Refining and marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Refining and marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aral.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aral.JPG/220px-Aral.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aral.JPG/330px-Aral.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Aral.JPG/440px-Aral.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aral.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Aral_AG" title="Aral AG">Aral</a> service station in Weiterstadt, Germany</div></div></div>
<p>BP downstream's activities include the refining, marketing, manufacturing, transportation, trading and supply of <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a>, petrochemicals and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_product" title="Petroleum product">petroleum products</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2012_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2012-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Downstream is responsible for BP's fuels, lubricants and petrochemical businesses and has major operations located in Europe, North America and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersProfile2012_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersProfile2012-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  December 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> BP owned or had a share in 11&#160;refineries and 17&#160;petrochemical manufacturing plants worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_BP_refining_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_BP_refining-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> The Company had sold or converted 16&#160;plants since 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_BP_refining_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_BP_refining-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> It is looking to sell off its stake in a petrochemicals joint venture in China, its largest investment in that country.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_BP_refining_228-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_BP_refining-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> *The company's petrochemicals plants produce products including PTA, paraxylene, and acetic acid.<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-downstream_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-downstream-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Its petrochemicals are marketed in over 40&#160;countries.<sup id="cite_ref-AR15-worldwide_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR15-worldwide-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP, which employs about 1,800&#160;people in oil trading and trades over 5 million barrels per day (790<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>3</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of oil and refined products, is the world's third biggest oil trader after <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vitol" title="Vitol">Vitol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_BP_trading_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_BP_trading-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> The operation is estimated to be able to generate over $1&#160;billion trading profits in a good year.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_BP_trading_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_BP_trading-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Air_BP" title="Air BP">Air BP</a> is the aviation division of BP, providing <a href="/wiki/Aviation_fuel" title="Aviation fuel">aviation fuel</a>, lubricants &amp; services. It has operations in over 50&#160;countries worldwide. <a href="/wiki/BP_Shipping" title="BP Shipping">BP Shipping</a> provides the logistics to move BP's oil and gas cargoes to market, as well as marine structural assurance.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>  It manages a large fleet of vessels most of which are held on long-term operating leases. BP Shipping's chartering teams based in London, Singapore, and Chicago also charter third party vessels on both time charter and voyage charter basis.  The BP-managed fleet consists of <a href="/wiki/Very_Large_Crude_Carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Very Large Crude Carrier">Very Large Crude Carriers</a> (VLCCs), one North Sea shuttle tanker, medium size crude and product carriers, <a href="/wiki/LNG_carrier" title="LNG carrier">liquefied natural gas (LNG) carriers</a>, <a href="/wiki/LPG_carrier" title="LPG carrier">liquefied petroleum gas (LPG) carriers</a>, and coasters. All of these ships are double-hulled.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP markets <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_product" title="Petroleum product">petroleum products</a> in more than 50&#160;countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-AR15-worldwide_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR15-worldwide-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> It has around 18,300&#160;service stations.<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-glance_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-glance-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Its flagship retail brand is BP Connect, a chain of service stations combined with a convenience store,<sup id="cite_ref-BPServiceStations_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPServiceStations-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> although in the US it is gradually being transitioned to the <a href="/wiki/Ampm" title="Ampm">ampm</a> format. In Germany and Luxembourg, BP operates service stations under the <a href="/wiki/Aral_AG" title="Aral AG">Aral</a> brand.<sup id="cite_ref-BPAral_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPAral-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>  On the US West Coast, in the states of California, Oregon, Washington, Nevada, Idaho, Arizona, and Utah, BP primarily operates service stations under the ARCO brand.<sup id="cite_ref-BPArco_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPArco-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>  In Australia BP operates a number of BP Travel Centres, large-scale destination sites located which, in addition to the usual facilities in a BP Connect site, also feature food-retail tenants such as <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a>, <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nando%27s" title="Nando&#39;s">Nando's</a> and facilities for long-haul truck drivers.<sup id="cite_ref-BP_Truck_Stop_Australia_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP_Truck_Stop_Australia-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Castrol" title="Castrol">Castrol</a> is BP's main brand for industrial and <a href="/wiki/Automotive" class="mw-redirect" title="Automotive">automotive</a> <a href="/wiki/Lubricants" class="mw-redirect" title="Lubricants">lubricants</a> and is applied to a large range of BP oils, <a href="/wiki/Grease_(lubricant)" title="Grease (lubricant)">greases</a> and similar products for most <a href="/wiki/Lubrication" title="Lubrication">lubrication</a> applications.<sup id="cite_ref-BPCastrol_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPCastrol-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, BP owned or had a share in 11&#160;refineries<sup id="cite_ref-AR17-refining_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR17-refining-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> and 15&#160;petrochemical manufacturing plants worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Plants17_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plants17-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_and_low_carbon_energy">Alternative and low carbon energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Alternative and low carbon energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SolarpanelBp.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SolarpanelBp.JPG/220px-SolarpanelBp.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SolarpanelBp.JPG/330px-SolarpanelBp.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/SolarpanelBp.JPG/440px-SolarpanelBp.JPG 2x" data-file-width="532" data-file-height="299" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SolarpanelBp.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A BP photovoltaic (PV) module that is composed of multiple PV cells. Two or more interconnected PV modules create an array.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg/220px-Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg/330px-Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg/440px-Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3880" data-file-height="2607" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm_2621902438.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm" title="Fowler Ridge Wind Farm">Fowler Ridge Wind Farm</a></div></div></div>
<p>BP was the first of <a href="/wiki/Supermajor" class="mw-redirect" title="Supermajor">supermajors</a> expanding its focus on energy sources other than fossil fuels.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters151217_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters151217-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> It established an <a href="/wiki/Alternative_energy" title="Alternative energy">alternative</a> and low carbon energy business in 2005, with plans to invest $8 billion over a 10-year period into renewable energy sources including solar, wind, and <a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a>, and non-renewable sources including <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen power">hydrogen power</a>. According to the company, it spent a total of $8.3 billion in these projects through completion in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Schiller-2012_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schiller-2012-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wells2012_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wells2012-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bpalternative_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpalternative-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bp_sustainability_review_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bp_sustainability_review-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  May 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, BP operated 13&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wind_farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind farms">wind farms</a> in seven states in the United States, and held an interest in another in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BP-wind_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP-wind-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>  These wind farms include the <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Creek_Wind_Farm" title="Cedar Creek Wind Farm">Cedar Creek Wind Farm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Titan_Wind_Project" title="Titan Wind Project">Titan Wind Project</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherbino_Wind_Farm" title="Sherbino Wind Farm">Sherbino Wind Farm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Hills_Wind_Project" title="Golden Hills Wind Project">Golden Hills Wind Project</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm" title="Fowler Ridge Wind Farm">Fowler Ridge Wind Farm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-platts030413_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-platts030413-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg030413_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg030413-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-csm040413_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csm040413-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>  As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the company had total gross generating capacity of 2.3&#160;GW of wind energy in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-spw201217_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spw201217-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>  In 2016, the company generated  4.389&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour#Multiples" title="Kilowatt hour">TW·h</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AR16-wind_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR16-wind-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Brazil, BP owns two ethanol producers—<i>Companhia Nacional de Açúcar e Álcool</i> and<i>Tropical BioEnergia</i>—with three ethanol mills.<sup id="cite_ref-bp-sugarcane_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bp-sugarcane-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters140911_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters140911-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> These mills produce around 800,000 cubic metres per annum (5,000,000&#160;bbl/a) of ethanol equivalent.<sup id="cite_ref-spw201217_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spw201217-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> BP has invested in an agricultural biotechnology company Chromatin, a company developing crops that can grow on marginal land and that are optimized to be used as feedstock for biofuel,<sup id="cite_ref-Herndon2011_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herndon2011-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> and Vedrezyne, which produces petrochemicals in <a href="/wiki/Yeast" title="Yeast">yeast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CheckBiotech2011_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CheckBiotech2011-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Its joint venture with DuPont called Butamax, which has developed the patented bio-butanol-producing technology<sup id="cite_ref-delaware280815_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delaware280815-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> and owns an isobutanol plant in <a href="/wiki/Scandia,_Kansas" title="Scandia, Kansas">Scandia, Kansas</a>, United States.<sup id="cite_ref-biomass030417_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biomass030417-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In addition BP owns biomethane production facilities in <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Michigan" title="Canton, Michigan">Canton, Michigan</a> and North Shelby, Tennessee as well as share of facilities under construction in <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City" title="Oklahoma City">Oklahoma City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hardcastle17_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hardcastle17-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> BP's subsidiary Air BP supplies aviation biofuel at <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen" title="Oslo Airport, Gardermoen">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halmstad_Airport" title="Halmstad Airport">Halmstad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bergen_Airport,_Flesland" title="Bergen Airport, Flesland">Bergen</a> airports.<sup id="cite_ref-aviationpross210817_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aviationpross210817-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Six years after closing down BP Solar, BP announced its return to the solar sector with an investment of $200 million to Lightsource Renewable Energy (Lightsource BP). Differently from BP Solar, Lightsource BP focuses on the managing and maintaining <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_power_station" title="Photovoltaic power station">solar farms</a> instead of manufacturing solar panels.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg151217_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg151217-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Lightsource has commissioned 1.3&#160;GW of solar capacity and manages about 2&#160;GW of solar capacity. It plans to increase the capacity up to 8&#160;GW through projects in the United States, India, Europe and the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters151217_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters151217-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP has invested $20&#160;million in Israeli quick-charging battery firm StoreDot Ltd.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg240518_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg240518-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, the CEO Bob Dudley said that out of the company's total spending of $15 to $17&#160;billion per year, about $500&#160;million will be invested in low-carbon energy and technology.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters210518_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters210518-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> The relatively small size of BP's alternative energy operations has led to allegations of <a href="/wiki/Greenwashing" title="Greenwashing">greenwashing</a> by <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mother_Jones_(magazine)" title="Mother Jones (magazine)">Mother Jones</a><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> and energy analyst and activist <a href="/wiki/Antonia_Juhasz" title="Antonia Juhasz">Antonia Juhasz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The chairman of the BP board of directors is <a href="/wiki/Carl-Henric_Svanberg" title="Carl-Henric Svanberg">Carl-Henric Svanberg</a> and the chief executive officer is <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dudley" title="Bob Dudley">Robert Dudley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Helge_Lund" title="Helge Lund">Helge Lund</a> is appointed as the chairman of the board of directors starting from 1 September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-sw260418_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sw260418-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ft260418_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft260418-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stock">Stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>BP stock is composed of original BP shares as well as shares acquired through mergers with <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a> in 1998 and the <a href="/wiki/ARCO" title="ARCO">Atlantic Richfield Company</a> (ARCO) in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1998_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1998-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNNMoney2000_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNMoney2000-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>  The company's shares are primarily traded on the London Stock Exchange, but also listed on the Frankfurt Stock Exchange in Germany. In the United States shares are traded in US$ on the New York Stock Exchange in the form of <a href="/wiki/American_depositary_receipt" title="American depositary receipt">American depository shares</a> (ADS). One ADS represents six ordinary shares.<sup id="cite_ref-BPShare_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPShare-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the United States <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a>'s approval of the BP-Amoco merger in 1998, Amoco's stock was removed from <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;P 500">Standard &amp; Poor's 500</a> and was merged with BP shares on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1998_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1998-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> The merger with Amoco resulted in a 40% increase in share price by April 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-Brierly1999_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brierly1999-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> However, shares fell nearly 25% by early 2000, when the Federal Trade Commission expressed opposition to BP-Amoco's acquisition of ARCO.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTFeb2000_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTFeb2000-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition was ultimately approved in April 2000 increasing stock value 57 cents over the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-CNNMoney2000_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNMoney2000-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the Texas City Refinery explosion in 2005, stock prices again fell. By January 2007, the explosion, coupled with a pipeline spill in Alaska and production delays in the Gulf of Mexico, left BP's stock down 4.5% from its position prior to the Texas City explosion.<sup id="cite_ref-Franklin2007_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Franklin2007-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> However, by April 2007, stocks had rebounded 13% erasing the 8.3% loss from 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Voss2007_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voss2007-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> Declining oil prices and concerns over oil sustainability also caused shares to fall in value in late 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Werdigier2008_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Werdigier2008-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Deepwater Horizon oil spill in April 2010 initiated a sharp decline in share prices, and BP's shares lost roughly 50% of their value in 50&#160;days.<sup id="cite_ref-SmithApril2011_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SmithApril2011-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> BP's shares reached a low of $26.97 per share on 25 June 2010 totalling a $100 billion loss in market value<sup id="cite_ref-Hays2010_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hays2010-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> before beginning to climb again. Shares reached a post-spill high of $49.50 in early 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-PeraltaJuly2012_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeraltaJuly2012-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 March 2013, BP announced an $8&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Share_repurchase" title="Share repurchase">share repurchase</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes220313_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes220313-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_04102013_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_04102013-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>  The buyback decision followed closure of the TNK-BP deal and it has to offset the dilution to earnings per share following the loss of dividends from TNK-BP.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_04102013_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_04102013-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>  The buyback was also seen as a way to invest excess cash from the TNK-BP deal.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_04102013_275-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_04102013-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  27&#160;May&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, major institutional shareholders include <a href="/wiki/BlackRock_Investment_Management_(UK)_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="BlackRock Investment Management (UK) Ltd.">BlackRock Investment Management (UK) Ltd.</a> (3.35% as of  14&#160;May&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>), The Vanguard Group, Inc. (3.12% as at 2 May 2018), Norges Bank Investment Management (2.21% as at 2 May 2018) and <a href="/wiki/Legal_%26_General_Investment_Management_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="Legal &amp; General Investment Management Ltd.">Legal &amp; General Investment Management Ltd.</a> (2.07% as of  2&#160;May&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-FTShareholders2012_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FTShareholders2012-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding_and_public_relations">Branding and public relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Branding and public relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the first quarter of 2001 the company adopted the marketing name of BP, and replaced its "Green Shield" logo with the "Helios" symbol, a green and yellow sunflower logo named after the <a href="/wiki/Helios" title="Helios">Greek sun god</a> and designed to represent energy in its many forms. BP introduced a new corporate slogan – "Beyond Petroleum" along with a $200M advertising and marketing campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-Ries_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ries-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Landman_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landman-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> According to the company, the new slogan represented their focus on meeting the growing demand for fossil fuels, manufacturing and delivering more advanced products, and to enable transitioning to a lower carbon footprint.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2008, BP's branding campaign had succeeded with the culmination of a 2007 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Effie_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Effie Award (page does not exist)">Effie Award</a> from by the <a href="/wiki/American_Marketing_Association" title="American Marketing Association">American Marketing Association</a>, and consumers had the impression that BP was one of the greenest petroleum companies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> BP was criticised by environmentalists and marketing experts, who stated that the company's alternative energy activities were only a fraction of the company's business at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Now" class="mw-redirect" title="Democracy Now">Democracy Now</a>, BP's marketing campaign amounted to a deceptive <a href="/wiki/Greenwashing" title="Greenwashing">greenwashing</a> public-relations <a href="/wiki/Spin_(public_relations)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spin (public relations)">spin campaign</a> given that BP's 2008 budget included more than $20 billion for fossil fuel investment and less than $1.5 billion for all alternative forms of energy.<sup id="cite_ref-Amy_Goodman_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amy_Goodman-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kempff_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kempff-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> Oil and energy analyst <a href="/wiki/Antonia_Juhasz" title="Antonia Juhasz">Antonia Juhasz</a> notes BP's investment in green technologies peaked at 4% of its exploratory budget prior to cutbacks, including the discontinuation of BP Solar and the closure of its alternative energy headquarters in London.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters211211_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters211211-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Amy_Goodman_282-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amy_Goodman-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>  According to Juhasz, "four percent...hardly qualifies the company to be Beyond Petroleum", citing BP's "aggressive modes of production, whether it's the tar sands [or] offshore".<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP attained a negative public image from the series of industrial accidents that occurred through the 2000s, and its public image was severely damaged after the Deepwater Horizon explosion and Gulf Oil spill. In the immediate aftermath of the spill, <a href="/wiki/Reactions_to_the_Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill#BP_public_relations" title="Reactions to the Deepwater Horizon oil spill">BP initially downplayed the severity of the incident</a>, and made many of the same PR errors that Exxon had made after the <i>Exxon Valdez</i> disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wired_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wired-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> CEO Tony Hayward was criticised for his statements and had committed several gaffes, including stating that he "wanted his life back."<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> Some in the media commended BP for some of its social media efforts, such as the use of Twitter and Facebook as well as a section of the company's website where it communicated its efforts to clean up the spill.<sup id="cite_ref-Slate2010_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slate2010-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP began a re-branding campaign in late 2010, and decided to focus its brand on the idea of "bringing brilliant minds together with technology at a massive scale to meet the world's energy needs", and focus its messaging on telling stories about people.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> In February 2012 BP North America launched a $500 million branding campaign to rebuild its brand.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company's advertising budget was about $5 million per week during the four-month spill in the Gulf of Mexico, totaling nearly $100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, BP tasked a press office staff member to openly join discussions on the Wikipedia article's talk page and suggest content to be posted by other editors.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> Controversy emerged in 2013 over the amount of content from BP that had entered this article.<sup id="cite_ref-zdnet2013_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zdnet2013-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Wikipedia co-founder <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Wales" title="Jimmy Wales">Jimmy Wales</a> stated that, by identifying himself as a BP staff member, the contributor in question had complied with site policy regarding conflicts of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-zdnet2013_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zdnet2013-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBTQ_recognition">LGBTQ recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: LGBTQ recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, BP backed a global study researching challenges for lesbian, gay, bisexual and transgender employees and for ways that companies can be a "force for change" for LGBT workers around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FT14_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT14-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> wrote that BP is "known for their more liberal policies for gay and transgender workers".<sup id="cite_ref-Driver15_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Driver15-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> A 2016 article in the <i>Houston Chronicle</i> said BP was "among the first major companies in the United States to offer LGBT workers equal protection and benefits roughly 20 years ago".<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> BP scored a 100 percent on the 2018 Human Rights Campaign's Corporate Equality Index, which was released in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-EqualityIndex18_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EqualityIndex18-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2017, BP added gender reassignment surgery to its list of benefits for U.S. employees.<sup id="cite_ref-Hunn17_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunn17-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> According to the Human Rights Campaign, BP is one of only a few oil and gas companies offering transgender benefits to its employees.<sup id="cite_ref-Hunn17_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunn17-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> BP ranked No. 51 on the list of Top 100 employers for lesbian, gay, bisexual and transgender staff on the 2017 Stonewall Workplace Equality Index.<sup id="cite_ref-SWEI_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SWEI-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2017, John Mingé, chairman and president of BP America, signed a letter alongside other Houston oil executives denouncing the proposed "bathroom bill" in Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-Andrews17_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andrews17-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_rights">Indigenous rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Indigenous rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>BP has been ranked as among the 15th best of 92 oil, gas, and mining companies on indigenous rights and resource extraction in the Arctic.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Position_on_global_warming">Position on global warming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Position on global warming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1997, BP became the first multinational outside the reinsurance industry to publicly support the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_consensus_on_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific consensus on climate change">scientific consensus on climate change</a>, which Eileen Caussen, President of the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Center_on_Global_Climate_Change" class="mw-redirect" title="Pew Center on Global Climate Change">Pew Center on Global Climate Change</a> described as a transformative moment on the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Prior to 1997, BP was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Climate_Coalition" title="Global Climate Coalition">Global Climate Coalition</a> an industry organisation established to promote <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_scepticism" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming scepticism">global warming scepticism</a> but withdrew in 1997, saying "the time to consider the policy dimensions of climate change is not when the link between greenhouse gases and climate change is conclusively proven, but when the possibility cannot be discounted and is taken seriously by the society of which we are part. We in BP have reached that point.".<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stanford_GSB_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanford_GSB-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> In March 2002, Lord John Browne, the group chief executive of BP, declared in a speech that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> was real and that urgent action was needed.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> According to a <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">New York Times</a></i> article, BP was "at the forefront when it came to major oil companies going green" due to its investments in renewables, and acknowledgement of the connection between fossil fuel consumption and global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Hazardous_substance_dumping_1993.E2.80.931995"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hazardous_substance_dumping_1993–1995"><span id="1993.E2.80.931995:_Hazardous_substance_dumping"></span>Hazardous substance dumping 1993–1995</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Hazardous substance dumping 1993–1995">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 1999, one of BP's US subsidiaries, BP Exploration Alaska (BPXA), pleaded guilty to criminal charges stemming from its illegally dumping of hazardous wastes on the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_North_Slope" title="Alaska North Slope">Alaska North Slope</a>, paying fines and penalties totaling $22&#160;million. BP paid the maximum $500,000 in criminal fines, $6.5&#160;million in civil penalties, and established a $15&#160;million environmental management system at all of BP facilities in the US and Gulf of Mexico that are engaged in oil exploration, drilling or production. The charges stemmed from the 1993 to 1995 dumping of hazardous wastes on <a href="/wiki/Endicott_Island" title="Endicott Island">Endicott Island</a>, Alaska by BP's contractor Doyon Drilling. The firm illegally discharged waste oil, paint thinner and other toxic and hazardous substances by injecting them down the outer rim, or annuli, of the oil wells. BPXA failed to report the illegal injections when it learned of the conduct, in violation of the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Environmental_Response,_Compensation_and_Liability_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation and Liability Act">Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation and Liability Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_pollution_violations">Air pollution violations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Air pollution violations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2000, BP Amoco acquired ARCO, a Los Angeles-based oil group.<sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
In 2003, California's <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_Air_Quality_Management_District" title="South Coast Air Quality Management District">South Coast Air Quality Management District</a> (AQMD) filed a complaint against BP/ARCO, seeking $319 million in penalties for thousands of air pollution violations over an 8-year period.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup>  In January 2005, the agency filed a second suit against BP based on violations between August 2002 and October 2004.  The suit alleged that BP illegally released air pollutants by failing to adequately inspect, maintain, repair and properly operate thousands of pieces of equipment across the refinery as required by AQMD regulations.  It was alleged that in some cases the violations were due to negligence, while in others the violations were knowingly and willfully committed by refinery officials.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, a settlement was reached under which BP agreed to pay $25 million in cash penalties and $6 million in past emissions fees, while spending $20 million on environmental improvements at the refinery and $30 million on community programs focused on asthma diagnosis and treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, a total of 474 <a href="/wiki/Galveston_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Galveston County">Galveston County</a> residents living near the BP Texas City Refinery filed a $1 billion lawsuit against BP, accusing the company of "intentionally misleading the public about the seriousness" of a two-week release of toxic fumes which began on 10 November 2011. "BP reportedly released Sulfur Dioxide, Methyl Carpaptan, Dimethyl Disulfide and other toxic chemicals into the atmosphere” reads the report. The lawsuit further claims Galveston county has the worst air quality in the United States due to BP's violations of air pollution laws. BP had no comment and said it would address the suit in the court system.<sup id="cite_ref-Courthouse-news-4-15-13_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Courthouse-news-4-15-13-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rice-April162013_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rice-April162013-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombian_farmland_damages_claim">Colombian farmland damages claim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Colombian farmland damages claim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, a group of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombian</a> farmers reached a multimillion-dollar out-of-court settlement with BP for alleged environmental damage caused by the <a href="/wiki/Ocensa_pipeline" title="Ocensa pipeline">Ocensa pipeline</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> An agreed statement said: "The Colombian farmers group are pleased to say that after a mediation process which took place in Bogotá in June 2006 at the joint initiative of the parties, an amicable settlement of the dispute in relation to the Ocensa pipeline has been reached, with no admissions of liability." The company was accused of benefiting from a regime of terror carried out by Colombian government paramilitaries to protect the 450-mile (720&#160;km) Ocensa pipeline; BP said throughout that it has acted responsibly and that landowners were fairly compensated.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, another group of 95&#160;Colombian farmers filed a suit against BP, saying the company's Ocensa pipeline caused landslides and damage to soil and groundwater, affecting crops, livestock, and contaminating water supplies, making fish ponds unsustainable. Most of the land traversed by the pipeline was owned by peasant farmers who were illiterate and unable to read the environmental impact assessment conducted by BP prior to construction, which acknowledged significant and widespread risks of damage to the land.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canadian_oil_sands">Canadian oil sands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Canadian oil sands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_articles_about_Canadian_oil_sands" title="List of articles about Canadian oil sands">List of articles about Canadian oil sands</a></div>
<p>In Canada, BP is involved in the extraction of oil sands, also known as tar sands or bituminous sands. The company uses <i>in-situ</i> drilling technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Steam-assisted_gravity_drainage" title="Steam-assisted gravity drainage">Steam Assisted Gravity Drainage</a> to extract the <a href="/wiki/Bitumen" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitumen">bitumen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BPCanadianOilSands_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPCanadianOilSands-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPOilSandsFAQ2012_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPOilSandsFAQ2012-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReutersJan2010_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersJan2010-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> Members of US and Canadian oil companies say that using recycled <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> makes in situ drilling an <a href="/wiki/Environmentally_friendlier" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmentally friendlier">environmentally friendlier</a> option when compared with oil sands mining.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Members of Canada's <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a> have criticized BP's involvement in the Canadian project for the impacts tar sands extraction has on the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Macalister2009_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macalister2009-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> NASA scientist <a href="/wiki/James_Hansen" title="James Hansen">James Hansen</a> said that the exploitation of Canadian tar sands would mean "game over for the climate".<sup id="cite_ref-The_New_York_Times_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, activist shareholders asked BP for a full investigation of the project, but were defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, shareholders criticized the project for being carbon-intensive.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Violations_and_accidents">Violations and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Violations and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Citing conditions similar to those that resulted in the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Texas_City_Refinery_explosion" title="Texas City Refinery explosion">Texas City Refinery explosion</a>, on 25 April 2006, the U.S. Department of Labor's <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">Occupational Safety and Health Administration</a> (OSHA) fined BP more than $2.4 million for unsafe operations at the company's <a href="/wiki/Oregon,_Ohio" title="Oregon, Ohio">Oregon, Ohio</a> refinery.  An OSHA inspection resulted in 32 per-instance willful citations including locating people in vulnerable buildings among the processing units, failing to correct depressurization deficiencies and deficiencies with gas monitors, and failing to prevent the use of non-approved electrical equipment in locations in which hazardous concentrations of flammable gases or vapors may exist.  BP was further fined for neglecting to develop shutdown procedures and designate responsibilities and to establish a system to promptly address and resolve recommendations made after an incident when a large feed pump failed three years prior to 2006.  Penalties were also issued for five serious violations, including failure to develop operating procedures for a unit that removes sulfur compound; failure to ensure that operating procedures reflect current operating practice in the Isocracker Unit; failure to resolve process hazard analysis recommendations; failure to resolve process safety management compliance audit items in a timely manner; and failure to periodically inspect pressure piping systems.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN-4-25-06_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-4-25-06-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, BP and several other major oil refiners agreed to pay $422 million to settle a class-action lawsuit stemming from water contamination tied to the gasoline additive <a href="/wiki/MTBE" class="mw-redirect" title="MTBE">MTBE</a>, a chemical that was once a key gasoline ingredient.  Leaked from storage tanks, MTBE has been found in several water systems across the United States. The plaintiffs maintain that the industry knew about the environmental dangers but that they used it instead of other possible alternatives because it was less expensive.  The companies will also be required to pay 70 percent of cleanup costs for any wells newly affected at any time over the next 30 years.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>BP has one of the worst safety records of any major oil company that operates in the United States. Between 2007 and 2010, BP refineries in Ohio and Texas accounted for 97 percent of  "egregious, willful" violations handed out by the U.S. Occupational Safety and Health Administration (OSHA). BP had 760 "egregious, willful" violations during that period, while Sunoco and Conoco-Phillips each had eight, Citgo two and Exxon had one.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC-5-2010_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC-5-2010-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>  The deputy assistant secretary of labour at OSHA, said "The only thing you can conclude is that BP has a serious, systemic safety problem in their company."<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A report in <i><a href="/wiki/ProPublica" title="ProPublica">ProPublica</a></i>, published in the <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i> in 2010, found that over a decade of internal investigations of BP's Alaska operations during the 2000s warned senior BP managers that the company repeatedly disregarded safety and environmental rules and risked a serious accident if it did not change its ways. ProPublica found that "Taken together, these documents portray a company that systemically ignored its own safety policies across its North American operations -- from Alaska to the Gulf of Mexico to California and Texas. Executives were not held accountable for the failures, and some were promoted despite them."<sup id="cite_ref-Lustgarten-6-2010_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lustgarten-6-2010-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Project_On_Government_Oversight" title="Project On Government Oversight">Project On Government Oversight</a>, an independent non-profit organization in the United States which investigates and seeks to expose corruption and other misconduct, lists BP as number one on their listing of the 100 worst corporations based on instances of misconduct.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1965_Sea_Gem_offshore_oil_rig_disaster">1965 Sea Gem offshore oil rig disaster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 1965 Sea Gem offshore oil rig disaster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sea_Gem" title="Sea Gem">Sea Gem</a></div>
<p>In December 1965, Britain's first oil rig, Sea Gem, capsized when two of the legs collapsed during an operation to move it to a new location. The oil rig had been hastily converted in an effort to quickly start drilling operations after the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> was opened for exploration. Thirteen crew members were killed.
