No hydrocarbons were released in the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dukeswood_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dukeswood-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_City_Refinery_explosion_and_leaks">Texas City Refinery explosion and leaks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Texas City Refinery explosion and leaks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The former <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a> oil refinery at <a href="/wiki/Texas_City,_Texas" title="Texas City, Texas">Texas City, Texas</a> was beset by environmental issues, including chemical leaks and a 2005 explosion that killed 15 people and injured hundreds. <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_News" title="Bloomberg News">Bloomberg News</a></i> described the incident, which led to a guilty plea by BP to a felony <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a> charge, as "one of the deadliest U.S. industrial accidents in 20 years." The refinery was sold to <a href="/wiki/Marathon_Petroleum" title="Marathon Petroleum">Marathon Petroleum</a> in October 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg-Texas_City_refinery_sale_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-Texas_City_refinery_sale-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_explosion">2005 explosion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 2005 explosion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Texas_City_Refinery_explosion" title="Texas City Refinery explosion">Texas City Refinery explosion</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg/220px-BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg/330px-BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg/440px-BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="504" data-file-height="334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BP_PLANT_EXPLOSION-1_lowres2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fire-extinguishing operations after the Texas City refinery explosion</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2005, the Texas City Refinery, one of the largest refineries owned then by BP, exploded causing 15&#160;deaths, injuring 180&#160;people and forcing thousands of nearby residents to remain sheltered in their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-McClatchy_Washington_Bureau_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClatchy_Washington_Bureau-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> A 20-foot (6.1&#160;m) column filled with hydrocarbon overflowed to form a vapour cloud, which ignited. The explosion caused all the casualties and substantial damage to the rest of the plant.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_12_July_2010_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_12_July_2010-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> The incident came as the culmination of a series of less serious accidents at the refinery, and the engineering problems were not addressed by the management. Maintenance and safety at the plant had been cut as a cost-saving measure, the responsibility ultimately resting with executives in London.<sup id="cite_ref-baker_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baker-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The fallout from the accident clouded BP's corporate image because of the mismanagement at the plant. There had been several investigations of the disaster, the most recent being that from the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Chemical_Safety_and_Hazard_Investigation_Board" title="U.S. Chemical Safety and Hazard Investigation Board">US Chemical Safety and Hazard Investigation Board</a><sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> which "offered a scathing assessment of the company." OSHA found "organizational and safety deficiencies at all levels of the BP Corporation" and said management failures could be traced from Texas to London.<sup id="cite_ref-McClatchy_Washington_Bureau_341-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClatchy_Washington_Bureau-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> The company pleaded guilty to a <a href="/wiki/Felony" title="Felony">felony</a> violation of the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a>, was fined $50&#160;million, the largest ever assessed under the Clean Air Act, and sentenced to three years probation.<sup id="cite_ref-justice.gov_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justice.gov-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 October 2009, the US <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">Occupational Safety and Health Administration</a> (OSHA) fined BP an additional $87&#160;million, the largest fine in OSHA history, for failing to correct safety hazards documented in the 2005 explosion. Inspectors found 270 safety violations that had been cited but not fixed and 439 new violations. BP appealed the fine.<sup id="cite_ref-McClatchy_Washington_Bureau_341-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClatchy_Washington_Bureau-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>  In July 2012, the company agreed to pay $13 million to settle the new violations. At that time OSHA found "no imminent dangers" at the Texas plant. Thirty violations remained under discussion.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters120712_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters120712-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> In March 2012, US Department of Justice officials said the company had met all of its obligations and subsequently ended the probationary period.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> In November 2011, BP agreed to pay the state of Texas $50 million for violating state emissions standards at its Texas City refinery during and after the 2005 explosion at the refinery. The state Attorney General said BP was responsible for 72 separate pollutant emissions that have been occurring every few months since March 2005. It was the largest fine ever imposed under the Texas Clean Air Act.<sup id="cite_ref-Florian-4-13_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Florian-4-13-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChronNov32011_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChronNov32011-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_toxic_substance_release">2007 toxic substance release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: 2007 toxic substance release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2007, 143 workers at the Texas City refinery claimed that they were injured when a toxic substance was released at the plant. In December 2009, after a three-week trial, a federal jury in Galveston awarded ten of those workers $10 million each in punitive damages, in addition to smaller damages for medical expenses and pain and suffering. The plant had a history of chemical releases.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_-_AP_-_Texas_refinery_-_2009_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_-_AP_-_Texas_refinery_-_2009-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup>  In March 2010, the federal judge hearing the case reduced the jury's award to less than $500,000. U.S. District Judge Kenneth M. Hoyt said the plaintiffs failed to prove BP was grossly negligent.<sup id="cite_ref-Chron_-_2010_Texas_City_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chron_-_2010_Texas_City-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_chemical_leak">2010 chemical leak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: 2010 chemical leak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In August 2010, the Texas Attorney General charged BP with illegally emitting harmful air pollutants from its <a href="/wiki/Texas_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Texas City">Texas City</a> refinery for more than a month.
BP has admitted that malfunctioning equipment lead to the release of over 530,000 pounds (240,000&#160;kg) of chemicals into the air of Texas City and surrounding areas from 6 April to 16 May 2010. The leak included 17,000 pounds (7,700&#160;kg) of <a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">benzene</a>, 37,000 pounds (17,000&#160;kg) of <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxides" class="mw-redirect" title="Nitrogen oxides">nitrogen oxides</a>, and 186,000 pounds (84,000&#160;kg) of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a>.  The State's investigation showed that BP's failure to properly maintain its equipment caused the malfunction.  When the equipment malfunctioned and caught fire, BP workers shut it down and routed escaping gases to flares. Rather than shut down associated units while compressor repairs were made, BP chose to keep operating those other units, which led to unlawful release of contaminants for almost 40 days.  The Attorney General is seeking civil penalties of no less than $50 nor greater than $25,000 per day of each violation of state air quality laws, as well as attorneys' fees and investigative costs.<sup id="cite_ref-ChronNov32011_350-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChronNov32011-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Attorney_General_of_Texas_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Attorney_General_of_Texas-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2012, over 50,000 Texas City residents joined a class-action suit against BP, alleging they became sick in 2010 as a result of the emissions release from the refinery. BP said the release harmed no one.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup>  In October 2013, a trial designed as a test for a larger suit that includes 45,000 people found that BP was negligent in the case, but due to the lack of substantial evidence linking illness to the emissions, decided the company would be absolved of any wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prudhoe_Bay">Prudhoe Bay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Prudhoe Bay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay_oil_spill" title="Prudhoe Bay oil spill">Prudhoe Bay oil spill</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg/220px-Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg/330px-Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg/440px-Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1446" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_prudhoe_bay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Prudhoe Bay</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2006, corrosion of a BP Exploration Alaska (BPXA) oil transit pipeline in <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Prudhoe Bay">Prudhoe Bay</a> transporting oil to the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System" title="Trans-Alaska Pipeline System">Trans-Alaska Pipeline</a> led to a five-day leak and the largest oil spill on <a href="/wiki/Alaska_North_Slope" title="Alaska North Slope">Alaska's North Slope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Roach2006_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roach2006-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> According to the Alaska Department of Environmental Conservation (ADEC), a total of 212,252 US gallons (5,053.6&#160;bbl; 803.46&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil was spilled, covering 2 acres (0.81&#160;ha) of the North Slope.<sup id="cite_ref-ADECMar2008_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADECMar2008-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> BP admitted that cost cutting measures had resulted in a lapse in monitoring and maintenance of the pipeline and the consequent leak. At the moment of the leak, <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_inspection_gauges" class="mw-redirect" title="Pipeline inspection gauges">pipeline inspection gauges</a> (known as "pigs") had not been run through the pipeline since 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-Rosen2007_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen2007-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Baltimore2007_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baltimore2007-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> BP completed the clean-up of the spill by May 2006, including removal of contaminated gravel and vegetation, which was replaced with new material from the Arctic tundra.<sup id="cite_ref-ADECMar2008_358-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADECMar2008-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Benschoten2006_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benschoten2006-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the spill, the company was ordered by regulators to inspect the 35 kilometres (22&#160;mi) of pipelines in Prudhoe Bay using "smart pigs".<sup id="cite_ref-Kleiner2006_364-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kleiner2006-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> In late July 2006, the "smart pigs" monitoring the pipelines found 16&#160;places where corrosion had thinned pipeline walls. A BP crew sent to inspect the pipe in early August discovered a leak and small spill,<sup id="cite_ref-Kleiner2006_364-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kleiner2006-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Isidore2006_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Isidore2006-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> following which, BP announced that the eastern portion of the Alaskan field would be shut down for repairs on the pipeline,<sup id="cite_ref-Isidore2006_365-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Isidore2006-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zibel2007_366-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zibel2007-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> with approval from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Transportation" title="United States Department of Transportation">Department of Transportation</a>. The shutdown resulted in a reduction of 200,000 barrels per day (32,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) until work began to bring the eastern field to full production on 2 October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Alaska_Update_367-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alaska_Update-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> In total, 23 barrels (3.7&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil were spilled and 176 barrels (28.0&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) were "contained and recovered", according to ADEC. The spill was cleaned up and there was no impact upon wildlife.<sup id="cite_ref-ADECAug2006_368-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADECAug2006-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the shutdown, BP pledged to replace 26 kilometres (16&#160;mi) of its Alaskan oil transit pipelines<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson2007_369-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson2007-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HeraldMar2008_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeraldMar2008-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> and the company completed work on the 16 miles (26&#160;km) of new pipeline by the end of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-BPPrudhoeBayFact_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPPrudhoeBayFact-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> In November 2007, BP Exploration, Alaska pleaded guilty to negligent discharge of oil, a misdemeanor under the federal <a href="/wiki/Clean_Water_Act" title="Clean Water Act">Clean Water Act</a> and was fined US$20&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-corrosion_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corrosion-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> There was no charge brought for the smaller spill in August 2006 due to BP's quick response and clean-up.<sup id="cite_ref-Rosen2007_359-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen2007-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> On 16 October 2007, ADEC officials reported a "toxic spill" from a BP pipeline in Prudhoe Bay comprising 2,000 US gallons (7,600&#160;l; 1,700&#160;imp&#160;gal) of primarily <a href="/wiki/Methanol" title="Methanol">methanol (methyl alcohol)</a> mixed with crude oil and water, which spilled onto a gravel pad and frozen tundra pond.<sup id="cite_ref-ktuu_373-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ktuu-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the settlement of a civil suit, in July 2011 investigators from the U.S. Department of Transportation's Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration determined that the 2006 spills were a result of BPXA's failure to properly inspect and maintain the pipeline to prevent corrosion. The government issued a Corrective Action Order to BP XA that addressed the pipeline's risks and ordered pipeline repair or replacement. The U.S. Environmental Protection Agency had investigated the extent of the oil spills and oversaw BPXA's cleanup. When BP XA did not fully comply with the terms of the corrective action, a complaint was filed in March 2009 alleging violations of the Clean Water Act, the Clean Air Act and the Pipeline Safety Act.  In July 2011, the U.S. District Court for the District of Alaska entered a consent decree between the United States and BPXA resolving the government's claims.  Under the consent decree, BPXA paid a $25 million civil penalty, the largest per-barrel penalty at that time for an oil spill, and agreed to take measures to significantly improve inspection and maintenance of its pipeline infrastructure on the North Slope to reduce the threat of additional oil spills.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-APMay32011_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APMay32011-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_Caspian_Sea_gas_leak">2008 Caspian Sea gas leak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 2008 Caspian Sea gas leak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 17 September 2008, a small gas leak was discovered and one gas-injection well broached to surface in the area of the Central Azeri platform at the <a href="/wiki/Azeri_oilfield" title="Azeri oilfield">Azeri oilfield</a>, a part of the <a href="/wiki/Azeri%E2%80%93Chirag%E2%80%93Guneshli" class="mw-redirect" title="Azeri–Chirag–Guneshli">Azeri–Chirag–Guneshli</a> (ACG) project, in the Azerbaijan sector of <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters170908_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters170908-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-time181210_377-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time181210-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup> The platform was shut down and the staff was evacuated.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters170908_376-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters170908-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg170908_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg170908-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup> As the West Azeri Platform was being powered by a cable from the Central Azeri Platform, it was also shut down.<sup id="cite_ref-wikileaks081008_379-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wikileaks081008-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> Production at the West Azeri Platform resumed on 9 October 2008 and at the Central Azeri Platform in December 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters101008_380-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters101008-380">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters231208_381-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters231208-381">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup> According to leaked US Embassy cables, BP had been "exceptionally circumspect in disseminating information" and showed that BP thought the cause for the blowout was a bad cement job. The cables further said that some of BP's ACG partners complained that the company was so secretive that it was withholding information even from them.<sup id="cite_ref-time181210_377-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time181210-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wikileaks150109_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wikileaks150109-383">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="California_storage_tanks">California storage tanks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: California storage tanks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Santa Barbara County District Attorney sued BP West Coast Products LLC, BP Products North America, Inc., and Atlantic Richfield Company over allegations that the companies violated state laws regarding operating and maintaining motor vehicle fuel underground storage tank laws. BP settled a lawsuit for $14 million. The complaint alleged that BP failed to properly inspect and maintain underground tanks used to store gasoline for retail sale at approximately 780 gas stations in California over a period of ten years and violated other hazardous material and hazardous waste laws.  The case settled in November 2016 and was the result of collaboration among the California Attorney General's Office and several district attorney's offices across the state.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deepwater_Horizon_explosion_and_oil_spill"><i>Deepwater Horizon</i> explosion and oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Deepwater Horizon explosion and oil spill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a> searches for missing crew</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bay_Jimmy,_Plaquemines_Parish_(9152010).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bay_Jimmy%2C_Plaquemines_Parish_%289152010%29.jpg/220px-Bay_Jimmy%2C_Plaquemines_Parish_%289152010%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bay_Jimmy%2C_Plaquemines_Parish_%289152010%29.jpg/330px-Bay_Jimmy%2C_Plaquemines_Parish_%289152010%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bay_Jimmy%2C_Plaquemines_Parish_%289152010%29.jpg/440px-Bay_Jimmy%2C_Plaquemines_Parish_%289152010%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bay_Jimmy,_Plaquemines_Parish_(9152010).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Heavy oiling of Bay Jimmy, Plaquemines Parish; 15 September 2010</div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Striped_Dolphins.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Striped_Dolphins.jpg/220px-Striped_Dolphins.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Striped_Dolphins.jpg/330px-Striped_Dolphins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Striped_Dolphins.jpg/440px-Striped_Dolphins.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1290" data-file-height="860" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Striped_Dolphins.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Striped dolphins (<a href="/wiki/Stenella_coeruleoalba" class="mw-redirect" title="Stenella coeruleoalba">Stenella coeruleoalba</a>) observed in emulsified oil on 29 April 2010</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill"><i>Deepwater Horizon</i> oil spill</a> was a major industrial accident on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, which killed 11&#160;people and injured 16&#160;others, leaked about 4.9 million barrels (210&#160;million US&#160;gal; 780,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil with plus or minus 10% uncertainty,<sup id="cite_ref-report2011_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2011-386">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup> which makes it the largest accidental marine oil spill in the history of the petroleum industry,<sup id="cite_ref-AccidentalRelease_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccidentalRelease-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MHL_387-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MHL-387">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup> and cost to the company more than $65&#160;billion of cleanup costs, charges and penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters160118_388-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters160118-388">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ft010518_389-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft010518-389">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup>  On 20 April 2010, the semi-submersible exploratory offshore drilling rig <i><a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon" title="Deepwater Horizon">Deepwater Horizon</a></i> located in the <a href="/wiki/Macondo_Prospect" title="Macondo Prospect">Macondo Prospect</a> in the Gulf of Mexico <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_explosion" title="Deepwater Horizon explosion">exploded</a> after a <a href="/wiki/Blowout_(well_drilling)" title="Blowout (well drilling)">blowout</a>. After burning for two days, the rig sank. The well was finally capped on 15 July 2010. Of 4.9 million barrels (210&#160;million US&#160;gal; 780,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of leaked oil 810,000 barrels (34&#160;million US&#160;gal; 129,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) was collected or burned while 4.1 million barrels (170&#160;million US&#160;gal; 650,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) entered the Gulf waters.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters220213_390-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters220213-390">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chron270413_391-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chron270413-391">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup>  1.8&#160;million US gallons (6,800&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of <a href="/wiki/Corexit" title="Corexit">Corexit</a> dispersant was applied.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The spill had a strong economic impact on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Coast">Gulf Coast</a>'s economy sectors such as fishing and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup>  As of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the fishing industry continued to struggle.<sup id="cite_ref-vice190415_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vice190415-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> A 2013 study in the <i>Journal of Travel Research</i> found that the hotel industry weathered the spill better than the vacation rental industry, and that the overall impact was complex and difficult to determine.<sup id="cite_ref-Journal_of_Travel_Research_396-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Journal_of_Travel_Research-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Environmental impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Oil spill caused damages across a range of species and habitats in the Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-ainsworth_397-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ainsworth-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup> Researchers say the oil and dispersant mixture, including <a href="/wiki/Polycyclic_aromatic_hydrocarbon" title="Polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbon">PAHs</a>, permeated the <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">food chain</a> through <a href="/wiki/Zooplankton" title="Zooplankton">zooplankton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-174_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-174-398">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ortmann_399-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ortmann-399">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-187_400-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-187-400">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup> Toxicological effects have been documented in <a href="/wiki/Benthic" class="mw-redirect" title="Benthic">benthic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pelagic" class="mw-redirect" title="Pelagic">pelagic</a> fish, <a href="/wiki/Estuarine" class="mw-redirect" title="Estuarine">estuarine</a> communities, mammals, birds and turtles, deep-water corals, plankton, <a href="/wiki/Foraminifera" title="Foraminifera">foraminifera</a>, and microbial communities. Effects on different populations consist of increased mortality or as sub-lethal impairment on the organisms' ability to forage, reproduce and avoid predators.<sup id="cite_ref-ainsworth_397-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ainsworth-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup>  In 2013, it was reported that dolphins and other marine life continued to die in record numbers with infant dolphins dying at six times the normal rate,<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> and half the <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> examined in a December 2013 study were seriously ill or dying. BP said the report was “inconclusive as to any causation associated with the spill."<sup id="cite_ref-dolphins-huffpo-2-14_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dolphins-huffpo-2-14-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Independent-dolphins-2-14_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-dolphins-2-14-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies in 2013 suggested that as much as one-third of the released oil remains in the gulf. Further research suggested that the oil on the bottom of the seafloor was not degrading.<sup id="cite_ref-bathtub_404-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bathtub-404">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup> Oil in affected coastal areas increased erosion due to the death of mangrove trees and marsh grass.<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dermansky_4-20-13_406-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dermansky_4-20-13-406">&#91;406&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">&#91;407&#93;</a></sup> As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, removal of oily material from the beaches of Louisiana and Florida continued.<sup id="cite_ref-npr211213_408-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr211213-408">&#91;408&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tbt230813_409-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbt230813-409">&#91;409&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">&#91;410&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Researchers looking at sediment, seawater, biota, and seafood found toxic compounds in high concentrations that they said was due to the added oil and dispersants.<sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-411">&#91;411&#93;</a></sup> Although Gulf fisheries recovered in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA-2011_fisheries_412-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-2011_fisheries-412">&#91;412&#93;</a></sup> a 2014 study of the effects of the oil spill on <a href="/wiki/Bluefin_tuna" title="Bluefin tuna">bluefin tuna</a> by researchers at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a>, published in the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i>, found that toxins released by the oil spill sent fish into cardiac arrest. The study found that even very low concentrations of crude oil can slow the pace of fish heartbeats. BP disputed the study, which was conducted as part of the federal Natural Resource Damage Assessment process required by the Oil Pollution Act.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes-fish-toxins_413-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-fish-toxins-413">&#91;413&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NOLA_2-14_414-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOLA_2-14-414">&#91;414&#93;</a></sup> The study also found that oil already broken down by wave action and chemical dispersants was more toxic than fresh oil.<sup id="cite_ref-Australian_-_2014_bluefin_study_415-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australian_-_2014_bluefin_study-415">&#91;415&#93;</a></sup> Another peer-reviewed study, released in March 2014 and conducted by 17 scientists from the United States and Australia and published in <i>Proceedings of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a></i>, found that tuna and amberjack that were exposed to oil from the spill developed deformities of the heart and other organs. BP responded that the concentrations of oil in the study were a level rarely seen in the Gulf, but <i>The New York Times</i> reported that the BP statement was contradicted by the study.<sup id="cite_ref-Wines-24-March-14_416-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wines-24-March-14-416">&#91;416&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_human_health">Effects on human health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Effects on human health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Research discussed at a 2013 conference included preliminary results of an ongoing study being done by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Environmental_Health_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="National Institute for Environmental Health Sciences">National Institute for Environmental Health Sciences</a> indicating that oil spill cleanup workers carry <a href="/wiki/Biomarkers" class="mw-redirect" title="Biomarkers">biomarkers</a> of chemicals contained in the spilled oil and the dispersants used.<sup id="cite_ref-nola220113_417-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nola220113-417">&#91;417&#93;</a></sup>  A separate study is following the health issues of women and children affected by the spill.  Several studies found that a "significant percentage" of Gulf residents reported mental health problems such as anxiety, depression and <a href="/wiki/PTSD" class="mw-redirect" title="PTSD">PTSD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nola220113_417-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nola220113-417">&#91;417&#93;</a></sup> According to a <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> study investigating the health effects among children living less than 10 miles from the coast, more than a third of the parents report physical or mental health symptoms among their children.<sup id="cite_ref-nola220113_417-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nola220113-417">&#91;417&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Australia's <i><a href="/wiki/60_Minutes_(Australian_TV_program)" title="60 Minutes (Australian TV program)">60 Minutes</a></i> reported that people living along the gulf coast were becoming sick from the mixture of Corexit and oil.<sup id="cite_ref-418" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-418">&#91;418&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Susan_D._Shaw" title="Susan D. Shaw">Susan Shaw</a>, of the <i>Deepwater Horizon</i> oil spill Strategic Sciences Working Group, says "BP told the public that Corexit was 'as harmless as Dawn dishwashing liquid'...But BP and the EPA clearly knew about the toxicity of the Corexit long before this spill." According to Shaw, BP's own safety sheet on Corexit says that there are "high and immediate human health hazards".<sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">&#91;419&#93;</a></sup> Cleanup workers were not provided safety equipment by the company, and the safety manuals were "rarely if ever" followed, or distributed to workers, according to a <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a> investigation. The safety manuals read: "Avoid breathing vapor" and "Wear suitable protective clothing."<sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-420">&#91;420&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-421" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-421">&#91;421&#93;</a></sup> Oil clean up workers reported that they were not allowed to use respirators, and that their jobs were threatened if they did.<sup id="cite_ref-422" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-422">&#91;422&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-423" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-423">&#91;423&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-424" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-424">&#91;424&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A peer-reviewed study published in <i><a href="/wiki/The_American_Journal_of_Medicine" title="The American Journal of Medicine">The American Journal of Medicine</a></i> reported significantly altered blood profiles of individuals exposed to the spilled oil and dispersants that put them at increased risk of developing liver cancer, leukemia and other disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-425" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-425">&#91;425&#93;</a></sup> BP disputed its methodology and said other studies supported its position that dispersants did not create a danger to health.<sup id="cite_ref-BP_gulf_website_-_Nov_13_2013_426-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP_gulf_website_-_Nov_13_2013-426">&#91;426&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, a study was published in  <i>Proceedings of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a></i> which found heart deformities in fish exposed to oil from the spill. The researchers said that their results probably apply to humans as well as fish.<sup id="cite_ref-Wines-24-March-14_416-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wines-24-March-14-416">&#91;416&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_and_criminal_suits">Civil and criminal suits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Civil and criminal suits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 15 December 2010, the Department of Justice filed a civil and criminal suit against BP and other defendants for violations under the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Water_Act" title="Clean Water Act">Clean Water Act</a> in the U.S. District Court for the Eastern District of Louisiana.<sup id="cite_ref-427" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-427">&#91;427&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-428" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-428">&#91;428&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>70</span></sup>  The case was consolidated with about 200 others, including those brought by state governments, individuals, and companies under Multi-District Litigation docket MDL No. 2179, before U.S. District Judge <a href="/wiki/Carl_Barbier" title="Carl Barbier">Carl Barbier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-429" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-429">&#91;429&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-430" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-430">&#91;430&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2012, BP and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Department of Justice</a> reached a $4 billion settlement of all federal criminal charges related to the explosion and spill.  Under the settlement, BP agreed to plead guilty to 11&#160;felony counts of manslaughter, two misdemeanors, and a felony count of lying to Congress and agreed to four years of government monitoring of its safety practices and ethics.  BP also paid  $525 million to settle civil charges by the Securities and Exchange Commission that it misled investors about the flow rate of oil from the well.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes2012-11_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes2012-11-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-431" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-431">&#91;431&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, the US government filed criminal charges against three BP employees; two site managers were charged with manslaughter and negligence, and one former vice president with obstruction.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes2012-11_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes2012-11-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the end of November 2012, the U.S. Government temporarily banned BP from bidding any new federal contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-432" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-432">&#91;432&#93;</a></sup> The ban was conditionally lifted in March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_3-14-14_433-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_3-14-14-433">&#91;433&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Judge Barbier ruled in the first phase of the case that BP had committed gross negligence and that "its employees took risks that led to the largest environmental disaster in U.S. history." He apportioned fault at 67% for BP, 30% for <a href="/wiki/Transocean" title="Transocean">Transocean</a> and 3% for <a href="/wiki/Halliburton" title="Halliburton">Halliburton</a>. Barbier ruled that BP was "reckless" and had acted with "conscious disregard of known risks."<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg-sept-5-14_434-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-sept-5-14-434">&#91;434&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Times_-_barbier_-_18_billion_435-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_-_barbier_-_18_billion-435">&#91;435&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Claims_settlement">Claims settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Claims settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In June 2010, after a meeting in the White House between President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and BP executives, the president announced that BP would pay $20 billion into a <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_Oil_Spill_Trust" title="Deepwater Horizon Oil Spill Trust">trust fund</a> that will be used to compensate victims of the oil spill. BP also set aside $100 million to compensate oil workers who lost their jobs because of the spill.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR_-_gulf_spill_fund_436-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_-_gulf_spill_fund-436">&#91;436&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_-_6-10-10_437-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_-_6-10-10-437">&#91;437&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 March 2012, BP and businesses and residents affected by the spill reached a settlement of roughly 100,000&#160;suits claiming economic losses. BP estimated that the settlement cost more than $9.2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2014_appeal_fail_438-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_appeal_fail-438">&#91;438&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-settleAP_439-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-settleAP-439">&#91;439&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, BP and five states agreed an $18.5&#160;billion settlement to be used for Clean Water Act penalties and various claims.<sup id="cite_ref-abc020715_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc020715-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_influence">Political influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Political influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lobbying_For_Libyan_Prisoner_Transfer_Release">Lobbying For Libyan Prisoner Transfer Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Lobbying For Libyan Prisoner Transfer Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>BP lobbied the British government to conclude a prisoner-transfer agreement which the Libyan government had wanted to secure the release of <a href="/wiki/Abdelbaset_al-Megrahi" title="Abdelbaset al-Megrahi">Abdelbaset al-Megrahi</a>, the only person convicted for the 1988 <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">Lockerbie bombing</a> over Scotland, which killed 270 people. BP stated that it pressed for the conclusion of prisoner transfer agreement amid fears that delays would damage its "commercial interests" and disrupt its £900 million offshore drilling operations in the region, but it said that it had not been involved in negotiations concerning the release of Megrahi.<sup id="cite_ref-440" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-440">&#91;440&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-441" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-441">&#91;441&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_contributions_and_lobbying">Political contributions and lobbying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Political contributions and lobbying">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2002, BP's then-chief executive, <a href="/wiki/Lord_Browne_of_Madingley" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Browne of Madingley">Lord Browne of Madingley</a>, renounced the practice of corporate <a href="/wiki/Campaign_contributions" class="mw-redirect" title="Campaign contributions">campaign contributions</a>, saying: "That's why we've decided, as a global policy, that from now on we will make no political contributions from corporate funds anywhere in the world."<sup id="cite_ref-442" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-442">&#91;442&#93;</a></sup> When the Washington Post reported in June 2010 that BP North America "donated at least $4.8 million in corporate contributions in the past seven years to political groups, partisan organizations and campaigns engaged in federal and state elections", mostly to oppose ballot measures in two states aiming to raise taxes on the oil industry, the company said that the commitment had only applied to contributions to individual candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-443" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-443">&#91;443&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 2008 U.S. election cycle, BP employees contributed to various candidates, with Barack Obama receiving the largest amount of money,<sup id="cite_ref-444" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-444">&#91;444&#93;</a></sup> broadly in line with contributions from Shell and Chevron, but significantly less than those of Exxon Mobil.<sup id="cite_ref-445" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-445">&#91;445&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, BP spent nearly $16 million <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a> the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-446" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-446">&#91;446&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, BP spent a total of $8,430,000 on lobbying and had 47 registered lobbyists.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_447-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-447">&#91;447&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Market_manipulation_investigations_and_sanctions">Market manipulation investigations and sanctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Market manipulation investigations and sanctions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/US_Justice_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="US Justice Department">US Justice Department</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commodity_Futures_Trading_Commission" title="Commodity Futures Trading Commission">Commodity Futures Trading Commission</a> filed charges against BP Products North America Inc. (subsidiary of BP plc) and several BP traders, alleging they conspired to raise the price of <a href="/wiki/Propane" title="Propane">propane</a> by seeking to <a href="/wiki/Corner_the_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Corner the market">corner the propane market</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-cftc_448-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cftc-448">&#91;448&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-msnbc290606_449-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc290606-449">&#91;449&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chron290111_450-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chron290111-450">&#91;450&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, one former trader pleaded guilty.<sup id="cite_ref-msnbc290606_449-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc290606-449">&#91;449&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, BP paid $303 million in restitution and fines as part of an agreement to defer prosecution.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters200412_451-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters200412-451">&#91;451&#93;</a></sup> BP was charged with cornering and manipulating the price of TET propane in 2003 and 2004. BP paid a $125 million civil monetary penalty to the CFTC, established a compliance and ethics program, and installed a monitor to oversee BP's trading activities in the commodities markets. BP also paid $53 million into a restitution fund for victims, a $100 million criminal penalty, plus $25 million into a consumer fraud fund, as well as other payments.<sup id="cite_ref-CFTC-2007_452-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFTC-2007-452">&#91;452&#93;</a></sup>  Also in 2007, four other former traders were charged. These charges were dismissed by a US District Court in 2009 on the grounds that the transactions were exempt under the Commodities Exchange Act because they didn't occur in a marketplace but were negotiated contracts among sophisticated companies. The dismissal was upheld by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Fifth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit">Court of Appeals for the 5th Circuit</a>
in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-chron290111_450-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chron290111-450">&#91;450&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2010, US regulators <a href="/wiki/FERC" class="mw-redirect" title="FERC">FERC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commodity_Futures_Trading_Commission" title="Commodity Futures Trading Commission">CFTC</a> began an investigation of BP for allegedly manipulating the gas market. The investigation relates to trading activity that occurred in October and November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian020211_453-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian020211-453">&#91;453&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters020211_454-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters020211-454">&#91;454&#93;</a></sup> At that time, CFTC Enforcement staff provided BP with a notice of intent to recommend charges of attempted market manipulation in violation of the Commodity Exchange Act. BP denied that it engaged in "any inappropriate or unlawful activity." In July 2011, the FERC staff issued a "Notice of Alleged Violations" saying it had preliminarily determined that several BP entities fraudulently traded physical natural gas in the Houston Ship Channel and Katy markets and trading points to increase the value of their financial swing spread positions.<sup id="cite_ref-naturalgasintel010811_455-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naturalgasintel010811-455">&#91;455&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> started an investigation into allegations the companies reported distorted prices to the price reporting agency <a href="/wiki/Platts" class="mw-redirect" title="Platts">Platts</a>, in order to "manipulate the published prices" for several oil and biofuel products.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters150513_456-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters150513-456">&#91;456&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ec140513_457-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec140513-457">&#91;457&#93;</a></sup> The investigation was dropped in December 2015 due to lack of evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg071215_458-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg071215-458">&#91;458&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Documents from a 2016 bid to drill in the Great Australian Bight revealed claims by BP that a large-scale cleanup operation following a massive oil spill would bring a "welcome boost to local economies."<sup id="cite_ref-massiveoilspill_459-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massiveoilspill-459">&#91;459&#93;</a></sup> In the same bid BP also stated that a diesel spill would be "socially acceptable" due to a lack of "unresolved stakeholder concerns."<sup id="cite_ref-massiveoilspill_459-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massiveoilspill-459">&#91;459&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A leaked email from mid 2017 was leaked in April 2018 in New Zealand. The email laid out that pricing was to be raised at certain sites around a region in order to regain volume lost at its Otaki branch.<sup id="cite_ref-460" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-460">&#91;460&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-AccidentalRelease-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-AccidentalRelease_11-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-AccidentalRelease_11-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Robertson, Campbell; Krauss, Clifford (2 August 2010). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2010/08/03/us/03spill.html">"Gulf Spill Is the Largest of Its Kind, Scientists Say"</a>. <i>The New York Times</i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
